Japanese Privy Council Approves Draft to Terminate Treaty

Notice to Be Issued After Christmas

(Tokyo) It is certain that the government's original plan to notify the termination of the Washington Naval Treaty will be approved at the Privy Council meeting on the 19th. The government has scheduled the final procedures to be decided at the cabinet meeting on the 21st. However, the date of issuing the notice will take time due to the arrangement of documents and other factors. Moreover, the US government and other countries are all on Christmas holiday, which is inconvenient. Therefore, the ending is that the issuance of the notice will be after Christmas on the 26th. (Domei, 18th)

(Tokyo) At 10 a.m. today, the Emperor personally opened the Privy Council's main meeting in the East Room of the Imperial Palace. The proposal to abandon the Washington Treaty was officially passed and handed over to the government on the same day. Therefore, the government convened a cabinet meeting, formally decided, and then requested the Emperor's approval. Then, Ambassador Saito in the United States notified the US State Department. The full text of the notice is as follows:

To Your Excellency, the Ambassador has the honor, according to the instructions of his government, to inform Your Excellency as follows: The Japanese government, in accordance with the provisions of Article 23 of the Treaty Limiting Naval Armaments signed in Washington on February 6, 1922, hereby notifies the Government of the United States of its intention to terminate the said Treaty. Hiroshi Saito, Japanese Ambassador to the United States, to His Excellency Cordell Hull, U.S. Secretary of State. (DenTsushin, 18th)

France's Attitude Towards Naval Treaty Remains Unchanged

Naval Budget 2.9 Billion Francs

(Paris) When the Senate discussed the naval budget bill this morning, the chairman of the Naval Committee, Lear, issued a statement saying that the German navy has made great progress, and France's maritime defense is seriously insufficient. He requested the government to find ways to amend the Washington Naval Treaty to expand France's original total tonnage of naval vessels. Naval Minister Pittly said with a smile that France has always believed that the Washington Treaty can only meet the needs of the time. As for Japan's request for France to jointly declare the termination of the treaty, the reason why it was not approved was because France did not want to embarrass Britain and did not want to create a sense of alienation. However, France's position on the Washington Naval Treaty is still the same as that explained in the Washington meetings in 1922. After the discussion, the Senate voted to pass the naval budget bill, with a total amount of 29.03 billion francs, an increase of 24 million francs compared to the previous naval budget. Espionage Panic in Singapore, Japanese Residences Searched

US Plans to Abandon Freedom of the Seas, Promote US-British Cooperation

International Supervision of Arms Easier to Achieve

Generally Considered a Prelude to US Joining League of Nations

(Washington) According to sources here today, the traditional American policy of freedom of the seas will be automatically abandoned under certain conditions in wartime. Senator Nye told the Associated Press today that he will introduce a bill to prohibit American merchant ships from flying the American flag when conducting commercial transactions with belligerent countries in wartime. The purpose of this proposal is to avoid the United States being dragged into future wars by protecting its people's neutral commerce. Nye also said that some aspects of the government strongly support his proposal, and when he announced this statement, Secretary of State Hull also recently stated that the State Department is studying the United States' neutral policy towards future wars. According to political observers, this proposed method is actually a prelude to the United States' revision or abandonment of the freedom of the seas policy, because the United States' participation in the European War was to maintain this policy. Some of President Roosevelt's advisors also believe that the United States should abandon this policy of demanding neutral rights for ships sailing to belligerent countries, because since 1812, the United States has repeatedly been drawn into international vortexes for this, and will be even more overwhelmed in the future. It is also heard that President Roosevelt himself is paying close attention to this matter. According to some observers, this is a natural result of the President's advocacy of limiting war profits and international control of arms transportation. Senator Nye also said that this move is also an expression of promoting international peace. There is much speculation here about whether the President, knowing that the public and congressional opinion support amending the American policy, will discuss it with other countries. Some even speculate whether the United States will propose this matter to Britain after the naval treaty is terminated, as a prerequisite for discussions between the two countries. (National Telegraph, 17th)

(London) The United States' traditional policy of "freedom of the seas," which it has insisted on in the past, is now likely to be abandoned. It is generally seen as the first step for the United States to join the League of Nations, because the views of London and Washington on the issue of the right of neutral ships to pass through war zones have always been very different, eventually leading to serious disputes. If the United States abandons this policy, then the international community will lose one of the opportunities for disputes. This move by the United States is of great interest here, but until diplomatic documents arrive, it is still considered to be exploratory in nature, to see how American public opinion moves. It is also not accidental that the United States has the idea of abandoning freedom of the seas at a time when the US Senate committee is investigating the arms trade, and a movement has arisen advocating international control of the arms trade. It can be asserted that if Washington wants to approach London on the issue of international control of the arms trade, British public opinion will certainly be happy to support it. We still remember Privy Councilor Baldwin's speech at the Conservative Party conference in Glasgow on November 24, in which he said that before the United States' attitude is clear, the British Navy can never independently impose an armed blockade on any country in the world. His meaning is that the claim to impose sanctions on aggressor countries, if the United States does not abandon the principle of freedom of the seas and insist on trading with belligerent countries, then blockading aggressor countries and imposing sanctions is tantamount to causing opposition from the United States. From this, it can be seen that if the principle of freedom of the seas is abandoned, then international supervision of the arms trade will inevitably be easier to achieve, and the United States will also be closer to the League of Nations. (Havas, 18th)

(London) The US State Department plans to submit a proposal to President Roosevelt, advocating that the principle of neutrality be completely revised, and that the principle of freedom of the seas, which the United States has always advocated, may also be abandoned. The British press believes that a change in the White House's views can be seen here. The Morning Post reported, "President Roosevelt's preparation to abandon freedom of the seas will have a good impact on British policy, or may promote Britain's participation in the European continental security plan. (According to the new principles proposed by the State Department, in the future, whenever war breaks out between other countries, if American ships risk sailing in combat waters, the American government will not protect them. In this way, whenever sanctions are implemented and aggressor countries' ports are blockaded, Britain will not need to take the United States into account and can do it freely.) Since the last 18 months, the United States' attitude has often been unexpected. This matter is even more unexpected to the general public. The abandonment of freedom of the seas is still an idea and has not become a concrete proposal, but Secretary of State Hull has already proposed research or has obtained President Roosevelt's approval. This matter is really worth paying attention to, because the traditional policy of the US government is to be significantly changed." The Daily Express said, "If this move by the United States becomes a reality, then the greatest potential for war between Britain and the United States will be eliminated. If Britain and the United States join hands, there will be no possibility of war in the world, and world peace will also have made great progress." (Havas, 17th)

New Canal to Be Dug in Nicaragua

Beneficial to US Commerce and Defense

Chairman of the Naval Committee Re-proposes Old Proposal

(Washington) Vincent, chairman of the House Naval Committee, has now put forward a proposal that was advocated 30 years ago to build a canal in Nicaragua to assist the Panama Canal. He said that the construction of the Nicaraguan Canal is necessary, because within five years, the locks of the Canadian canal will be too small to safely accommodate the new ships being built. Therefore, he advocates adopting the old plan to build this new canal, estimating that it will cost approximately 72.2 million yuan. The new canal is very beneficial in terms of commerce and national defense. He will discuss this matter with President Roosevelt soon. The general opinion of Congress is mostly in favor of building the Nicaraguan Canal. After this canal is built, it will be 172 miles long, from Clayton on the Atlantic coast via the Taizidu River, the San Juan River, and Lake Nicaragua to Brito on the Pacific coast, the most practical route. The United States had previously obtained the consent of the government of Nicaragua to send an engineering team of 400 people and a survey team led by Lieutenant General Jedwin, accompanied by two army and civil engineers, to measure the route connecting the two oceans. The survey showed that it was 177 miles long, 70 miles of which passed through Lake Nicaragua, and 55 miles passed through various rivers. This survey team returned to the country after completing its work in 1931. (Reuters, 17th)

(Washington) Lee, chairman of the House Subcommittee on the Panama Canal, stated today that there is no need for a canal connecting the Pacific and Atlantic Oceans through Nicaragua for at least 20 years, because there is no urgent need in terms of commerce, and it is not essential at this time in terms of military affairs. Lee's remarks were made in response to Congressman Vincent's announcement that he would propose the construction of the Nicaraguan Canal in Congress. Although there were repercussions in Tokyo today regarding the construction of the Nicaraguan Canal, Vincent remained silent, because the Tokyo Foreign Ministry called Vincent's "untimely declaration" a sign that the United States wants to dig this canal for strategic reasons, because the Panama Canal is sufficient to meet all commercial traffic needs. Vincent said today only that if his plan is passed by Congress, two points will be implemented first, namely, organizing a committee to study the canal route and its excavation costs. (National Telegraph, 17th)

International Police Force Continues to Enter Saar

No Resistance to Requisitioning of Civilian Housing

(Saarbrücken) Officers from various countries of the Saar International Police Force have been arriving here continuously. Their headquarters will be organized soon, including 27 British officers. Officers from Italy, the Netherlands, and Sweden will also participate. The first batch of the British contingent, totaling 200 men, will arrive tomorrow. The army is accompanied by 20 armored vehicles and many cars, which arrived in France on Sunday and are now heading towards the Saar region. The Saar Governing Commission has issued a special notice to the people of the Saar, stating that the entry of the International Police Force allows them to (1) requisition houses, land, residences, etc., regardless of whether they are owned by groups or individuals; (2) requisition civilian houses with furniture and supplies for officers; (3) requisition all supplies, food, utensils, services, etc. from civilians when necessary; (4) freely collect all kinds of transport from civilians. As for the soldiers living in private homes, it should be done in a way that does not disturb the order and convenience of the home. If there are any losses, the Governing Commission will compensate them in full. However, no one may refuse the requisition of goods, services, etc., otherwise they will be subject to a fine, or twice the value of the original requisitioned goods or services. (National Telegram, 17th)

The conference was initiated by the Department of Commerce and the National Association of Manufacturers. One faction advocated a pragmatic approach and a concrete plan, while the other faction advocated a cautious approach to the reconstruction issue. Former US Secretary of Commerce Stettinius asked the conference to pass a resolution supporting the President's power to deal with left-wing members of Congress. It is said that the President has expressed a willingness to cater to the interests of big businessmen, but if businessmen oppose the President, they will suffer the consequences. It is also said that businessmen must support the President in order to defeat left-wing members of Congress. (National Telegram, 17th)

Napoleon's Love Letters Auctioned

Three Hundred Letters Worth Ten Thousand Pounds

Purchased by the French Government

(London) An auction house here auctioned off several of Napoleon's love letters today, showing that Napoleon was indeed a passionate man. These letters were sent by Napoleon to Empress Marie Louise, totaling 318 letters, 112 of which were sent while he was in Russia. This proves Napoleon's passion. It is said that these letters have never been published before and are of great value. Last year, eight love letters from Napoleon to his lover Josephine were sold for a total of £4,400. The owner of the letters remains a secret, but it is said that they are preserved by the descendants of Empress Marie Louise, the Austrian Grand Duke. (National Telegram, 17th)

(London) The French government recently purchased 300 autograph letters from Napoleon I for £15,000, many of which have not been published. There is also a famous letter detailing the French war plan at the time. (Havas, 17th)

Poland and Germany Sign a Radio Broadcasting Agreement

(Warsaw Correspondence) Recently, the Polish and German radio administrations signed an agreement to exchange radio programs in order to promote the radio industry in both countries. The two sides now have closer contact in broadcasting programs. The stipulated programs include German romantic and classical music, as well as modern popular music, with occasional broadcasts of entire operas. In order to inform pilots of what is actually happening, the radio station also broadcasts detailed sports news and important news. This news is not only broadcast from the radio station, but also directly transmitted from sports fields, theaters, and concerts. Since the Polish and German radio industries signed this agreement, it is expected that other countries will follow suit, which will greatly contribute to the promotion of international friendship.

All Bandits in the Upper Reaches of the Min River Surrender Their Arms

(Fuzhou) The bandit group led by Chen Jiansheng, which had been causing trouble in the upper reaches of the Min River, with over 200 men and guns, was lured to various locations by the Security Special Service Regiment yesterday and surrendered all their arms. Dozens of bandits were killed on the spot, and over a hundred people, including Chen Jiansheng, were captured and will be escorted to the province for interrogation. (Special Telegram, 18th)

Survey of the Currency System in Sichuan Province

(Nanjing) Liu Xizhe, who went to Sichuan to investigate the currency system, reported that the Sichuan currency is roughly divided into (A) coins. Those that are relatively common throughout the province are (1) Sichuan Dragon Dollars of the Great Qing Dynasty, (2) Yuan Shikai silver dollars, (3) Sun Yat-sen silver dollars, (4) Sichuan-Yunnan half-yuan silver coins, and (5) Sichuan single and double silver coins. They are further divided by area. For example, Chengdu only uses Sichuan Dragon Dollars of the Great Qing Dynasty and Sichuan-Yunnan half-yuan coins. Sun Yat-sen silver dollars require a premium. Chongqing can use all of them because it is close to the Yangtze River. Jiangjin uses Sichuan Dragon Dollars of the Great Qing Dynasty and Yuan Shikai silver dollars. Those that use single silver coins do not use half-yuan silver coins. (B) There are dozens of types of copper auxiliary coins, ranging from 20 cash to 10,000 cash. The value varies from place to place, and the large number in circulation is impossible to calculate. The reason for the large number is the wars. In the past, every war in Sichuan took its expenses from the people. The people's strength was exhausted, and the financial resources were depleted. The military authorities then set up coin mints to cast copper coins. The value was not based on the composition, but on the marked number as the standard. For example, a copper coin the size of a square inch marked with 10,000 cash was used by the army as 10,000 cash, and one marked with 5,000 cash was used as 5,000 cash. Refusal to accept them was considered a crime. After the war, without military backing, the price fell. When the people used them to pay taxes, they still had to pay according to the market price. Therefore, the official minting price was one thing, and the market price was another. The official minting continued without stopping, and the currency system became more chaotic and beyond repair. (C) Auxiliary coins are divided into private bank deposit slips, village notes, and banknotes. In addition to the few banknotes issued by the Bank of China, the majority are deposit slips and village notes. All of the people's real estate can be mortgaged to private banks according to its value. The redeemer is responsible for the redemption, and the issuer takes a handling fee based on the chapter. The more deposit slips and village notes there are, the more chaotic the market finance becomes. (Special Telegram, 18th)

No New Year's Day Celebration with Foreign Delegation During National Crisis

(Nanjing) Because it is a time of national crisis, the National Government will not hold a New Year's Day celebration with the diplomatic corps this year, as it did last year. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has not only notified the foreign missions in Nanjing, but has also telegraphed its offices in Shanghai and Peiping to inform the foreign consulates in Shanghai and Peiping. Ministry of Finance Re-determines the Amount of Small Silver Coins, etc. that Passengers are Allowed to Carry

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Finance originally stipulated that each passenger was allowed to carry 10,000 copper coins. This has now been reduced to 5,000. The original limit for small silver coins, whether single or double, was 500. This has now been reduced to 300. Those who exceed this number must obtain a passport, otherwise it will be confiscated as smuggling. Since railway transport and passenger boats are not under the jurisdiction of the customs, the Ministry has specifically asked the railway bureaus and water police agencies to strictly investigate. Directors of Tax Bureaus May Not Be Elected as Executive Committee Members of Chambers of Commerce

(Nanjing) The Ministry of Industry and Commerce requested an interpretation of whether directors of tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus may be elected as executive committee members of chambers of commerce, whether directors of nitrate and sulfur bureaus may engage in commerce, and various other issues regarding representatives attending chambers of commerce. After deliberation, the Judicial Uniform Interpretation of Laws and Regulations Conference decided that all civil servants who receive salaries are subject to the regulations of the Civil Servant Service Regulations. Directors of tobacco and alcohol tax bureaus and directors of nitrate and sulfur bureaus are civil servants who receive salaries and should not engage in commerce or serve as representatives or staff members of chambers of commerce, whether directly or indirectly, in accordance with Article 10 of the Civil Servant Service Regulations. Although the nitrate and sulfur bureaus are under the jurisdiction of the Ministry of Military Affairs, the Ministry of Military Affairs is the primary agency of the administrative system, and the director of the nitrate and sulfur bureau is a civil servant engaged in public service and should be subject to the same laws and regulations as civil servants who receive salaries. If the person filling the position of director of the tax bureau is a contracting businessman, then it is a private contracting nature and cannot be regarded as a civil servant. (Special Telegram, 18th)

He Chengjun Leaves Nanjing to Return to Wuhan

Because she was friends with T. Bo, she met with disaster. (18th Special Dispatch)

How the car fell into the river is still unclear. International Commercial Telegram

Special Commercial Telegram from Reuters on December 18th

Gold and Silver ▲London Gold Price Today is 140 shillings and 9 pence, up 2 pence. ▲London Large Bars In the London silver market today, the spot price is 23 pence and 9375, and the futures price is 24 pence and 065, both down 3125. The price decline was due to six batches of sales from China and sales from India. Speculators bought in when the price fell, and the market stabilized at the close. ▲Mountrie Large Bars The Mountrie silver market opened weak, down 60 pounds, but soon recovered partially.

▲Bombay Large Bars The silver market opened steadily, then fell, and the close was quiet. The spot price was 64 rupees and 12 annas, down 10 annas.

Exchange Rate ▲US-UK The London foreign exchange market was stable this morning. The US-UK exchange rate opened at 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 3 fen, and 875 li, the same as yesterday's US-UK closing price. Sterling was stronger against the US dollar before noon. The latest exchange rate is 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 4 fen, and 25 li, 375 li higher than the opening price.

UK-France The opening price remained unchanged at 74 francs 84. It rose 6 pounds at 11:00 am to 74 francs 90, then remained unchanged.

US-UK The pound opened stronger in the New York foreign exchange market. The US-UK exchange rate was 4 yuan, 9 jiao, 9 fen, and 425 li, 375 li higher than yesterday.

Cotton and Wheat New York Cotton New York cotton opened sluggish, with little trading, but sentiment was good. It is reported that yarn factories do not have much cotton in stock. There are rumors that the managers of the cotton farmers' public storage agency are currently in Washington to discuss selling the stored cotton.

Chicago Wheat The opening price recovered slightly, up half a point. The same rise was seen in coarse grains. The domestic situation can be considered very stable.

Liverpool Cotton The cotton market was looser this morning. At 1:00 pm, the May futures price was 6.72, 3 pounds lower than yesterday's price.

Liverpool Wheat The wheat market was slightly stronger today. At 1:00 pm, the May futures price was 5 shillings, 2 pence, and 625 li, 25 li higher than yesterday's close.

Bombay Cotton The Bombay cotton futures market fell due to selling by European exporters and speculators. The market stabilized at the close. The price of B. Broach cotton for April-May delivery was 228 rupees and 75, 75 lower than yesterday.

Rubber London The rubber market was weak. The成交价格 for April-June delivery this afternoon was 6 pence and 5625 li.

New York The rubber market opened unchanged. Sentiment was stable, and prices rose slightly later.

Unfavorable factors for the market are the lukewarm attitude expressed by speculators. Sentiment was still stable when securities opened today, and price fluctuations were mostly limited to fractions. Constructive industrial and commercial news has already been discounted. Zhengzhong Bridge in Jiangxi to Break Ground Tomorrow

(Nanchang) The Zhengzhong Iron Bridge across the Gan River is scheduled to break ground on the 20th. An engineering supervision office has been established, and Wu Qiyou has been appointed as the chief engineer. (18th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Overseas Representatives Tour Hunan

(Changsha) Overseas Chinese representatives, including Wu Zhaohai and forty others, arrived in Hunan by express train from Hankou at 11:00 AM on the 16th. Representatives from various party, government, and military circles went to the station to welcome them. They stayed at the Provincial Government Guest House. At 9:00 AM on the 17th, the representatives attended the Sun Yat-sen Memorial Week at Zhongshan Hall and performed the rituals. Provincial Governor He Jian reported that Hunan Province has been peaceful since 1919 and welcomes overseas Chinese to visit and guide. He also stated that the roving bandits have been repeatedly intercepted by our troops, and many have been captured. Most of them have fled to Yongliping, Guizhou Province, and a portion are in Xinchang and Malukou, Tongjing, plotting to flee to Jinping, Guizhou. Our troops have defeated them and are currently pursuing them near the Guizhou border. I originally planned to go to Baoqing today to supervise the suppression, but because the overseas Chinese have come to Hunan from afar, I have postponed my trip. I still hope that the overseas Chinese can provide more guidance on the political construction of Hunan Province. It is greatly appreciated. The overseas Chinese representatives then gave a reply, and the meeting adjourned. At 10:00 AM, the representatives visited the National Products Exhibition Hall and the Black Lead Smelting Factory. At noon, Governor He hosted a banquet at the Provincial Government Guest House. In the afternoon, they visited the Soil Survey Institute. At 6:00 PM, all members of the Provincial Government hosted a banquet at the People's Martial Arts Club. At 7:00 PM, they watched a martial arts performance. It was also decided that on the morning of the 18th, they would visit the spinning mill and Hunan University, and tour the scenic spots of Mount Lu. In the afternoon, they would respond to the Provincial Party Headquarters' invitation. (17th Central News Agency Dispatch)

Xiamen Electric Boat Huihua Sinks

(Xiamen) The electric boat Huihua, carrying 500 barrels of gasoline, passengers, and about 60 crew members, sank in the Chicken Island sea area on the 18th at noon due to strong winds and heavy load, sailing from Xiamen to Shima. By evening, the Haicheng Water Patrol Team had only rescued 26 people, with more than 30 deaths. (18th Special Dispatch)

Copper Coins Surge in Xiamen

(Xiamen) Copper coins continue to surge in value. On the 18th, a small foreign coin could only be exchanged for 20 coins, a decrease of 4 coins compared to yesterday. A large foreign coin could be exchanged for 240 coins, a decrease of 45 coins compared to yesterday. Copper coins are being hoarded in the market, and transactions are sluggish, which has a great impact on small merchants and the working class. (18th Special Dispatch)

Public Telegram

Telegram from Kaifeng To the Editors of the Shanghai Shenbao: We are deeply surprised to read your newspaper's special dispatch from Nanjing on the 7th of this month stating that a breach of the Yellow River dike occurred half a li outside Puyang City in southern Hebei, rushing straight to the suburbs, with waves more than a zhang high over the city walls. Fortunately, the old Yellow River Jin Dike blocked the water, preventing it from reaching the city walls. However, the city is low-lying and there is a risk of it being submerged. The county magistrate is overseeing laborers day and night to rush to plug the Jin Dike. After investigating, this committee member was inspecting the project at Batou Jiugu Road on the 7th and 8th and did not hear of any breach of the Yellow River dike. When I instructed the Yellow River Affairs Bureau to investigate and reply, the steam telegram stated that the Jin Dike is half a li south of Puyang City. Currently, the water situation there is lower than before due to rush repairs to plug the breach, and there is no breach. Since this matter concerns the water situation and engineering conditions, the truth should be ascertained. We hereby telegraph your editorial department to investigate and make corrections to show the truth. We also hope to receive a reply. Respectfully, Kong Xiangrong, Member and Director of the Work Relief Group of the National Government Yellow River Flood Relief Committee.

Japanese Merchant Ship Smuggles Tax and Shoots at Inspectors

Japanese Ships Injure Many

Negotiations Between Both Sides in Beiping

Beiping Correspondence Since Shanhaiguan was occupied by the Japanese army, the gateway to China has been opened. Japanese merchants have taken the opportunity to freely trade goods and sell them in the interior of our country, resulting in an influx of Japanese goods in North China. After the closure of Shanhaiguan, tax cards were increased, and the import of Japanese goods by land was restricted. Qinhuangdao Customs has also strictly inspected due to changing circumstances. On the surface, there is no blatant leniency, but Japanese merchants are still overbearing, fearless, and deliberately smuggling goods. Moreover, smuggled goods are not directly unloaded and taxed in Tianjin, but are secretly transported by merchant ships to the Shihe area for transfer to the interior. On the 8th of this month, while inspectors from Qinhuangdao Customs were on patrol, they suddenly saw a Japanese merchant ship loaded with goods secretly transporting them to Shihe. They immediately stopped it and attempted to inspect it, but the merchant ship refused to be inspected and set up machine guns on the deck to shoot at the inspectors, injuring many people. Threatened by violence, the inspectors were unable to stop it and only copied the ship's number and reported it to Qinhuangdao Customs to find a way to negotiate. Acte, the Customs Commissioner of Qinhuangdao Customs, regarded Iwai, the head of the Japanese special affairs agency in Shanhaiguan, as unavailable, so he rushed to Beiping. He reported to the Political Affairs Readjustment Committee and negotiated with Iwai. Iwai immediately telegraphed to summon the important officials of the puppet organization customs, Uchida and Harada, to come to Beiping for inquiry. Uchida and Harada arrived in Beiping on the 13th and stayed at the Fusang Hotel on Chongwenmen Avenue. They went to the Beijing Hotel to meet Iwai and report everything. After hearing the report, Iwai visited Yin Tong on the 14th to exchange views. At noon today (15th), he invited relevant personnel from both sides to the Beijing Hotel to discuss solutions, including Yin Tong, Yin Rugeng, Acte Iwai, Uchida, Harada, and Fujiwara, the Superintendent of Postal Affairs of the puppet organization. The meeting lasted for about three hours. Our side focused on punishing the Japanese merchant ship and guaranteeing that such unfortunate events would not happen again in the future. The details of the discussion are not known. For the sake of facilitating contact, Iwai moved from the Beijing Hotel to the Fusang Hotel tonight (15th). Negotiations will continue tomorrow (16th). After both sides reach a result in Beiping, they will submit it to their superiors for approval. (December 15th)

Legislative Yuan Passes the County Autonomy Law

Chapter Six: County Government

Article 30: A county shall establish a county government, with one county magistrate elected by the county citizens' assembly, and reported to the superior authority for appointment.

Candidates for county magistrate shall be limited to those who have passed the central examination or qualification determination.

Article 31: The powers of the county magistrate are as follows: (1) To handle all county autonomous affairs under the supervision of the provincial government; (2) To execute matters entrusted by the central government and the province under the direction of the provincial government.

Article 32: The county government shall announce the county budget and final accounts, as well as county regulations decided by the county council.

Article 33: The county government may issue county orders within the scope of laws and regulations of the central government and the province.

Article 34: In case of extraordinary events, the county magistrate may request the provincial government to dispatch nearby troops and may directly request the commanders of such troops.

Article 35: The term of office of the county magistrate shall be three years, and may be re-elected.

Article 36: If the county magistrate violates the law or neglects his duty, he shall be removed from office by the county citizens' assembly.

Article 37: After the impeachment case is passed, the impeached county magistrate shall be dismissed immediately, and the county council shall appoint an acting county magistrate, who shall convene the county citizens' assembly within one month to elect a county magistrate, whose term of office shall be calculated from the date of election. The provisions of the preceding paragraph shall apply mutatis mutandis to the dismissal of a county magistrate after disciplinary action.

Article 38: The county government shall have the following departments:

Department One: In charge of the investigation and registration of household registration in the county, and land administration matters.

Department Two: In charge of the county's finances, public property, public utilities, and cooperative matters.

Department Three: In charge of the county's industry, transportation, water conservancy, and engineering construction matters.

Department Four: In charge of the county's security and public order matters.

Department Five: In charge of the county's education, culture, and preservation of scenic spots and historical sites.

Department Six: In charge of the county's conservation, relief, and health matters.

Other matters concerning county autonomy and the implementation of central administrative matters may be assigned by the county magistrate to the relevant departments for handling according to their nature.

Article 39: If necessary, the county government may, depending on the complexity of affairs and the amount of revenue, submit a proposal to the county council for resolution and, upon approval by the provincial government, appropriately change departments into bureaus, or reduce the number of merged departments.

Article 40: The county government shall have one secretary, one to four assistants, who shall guard the seals, handle confidential documents and general affairs, and other matters not specifically managed by the departments.

Article 41: Each department shall have one director and one to five staff members.

Article 42: The county government may employ specialized technical personnel and employees as needed.

Article 43: The organization of the county police or county defense corps shall be submitted by the county government to the provincial government for approval.

Article 44: The qualifications and procedures for the appointment of county government officials shall be determined separately.

Article 45: The county magistrate may convene county administrative meetings as necessary. The county magistrate shall be the chairman of the meeting.

The secretary, department heads, and relevant township and district chiefs shall attend the aforementioned meeting.

Article 46: The rules of procedure for county government affairs shall be determined by the Ministry of Interior.

Chapter Seven: County Finance

Article 47: The financial revenues of the county are as follows: (1) 70% or more of the county's land tax revenue; (2) 30% of the county's business tax revenue; (3) Revenue from county public property; (4) Revenue from county public utilities; (5) Other revenues that should be owned by the county according to law.

If the revenues in the preceding paragraphs are insufficient to cover expenditures, subsidies may be requested from the national treasury or the provincial treasury.

Article 48: At least 60% of the total amount of revenue in the preceding article shall be used for expenses for education, culture, economic construction, health care, conservation, relief, and other undertakings, and shall not be used for other purposes.

Article 49: County public property and county public enterprises shall not be mortgaged, sold, or used for private gain without the resolution of the county council and the approval of the provincial government.

Chapter Eight: Townships, Towns, and Districts

Article 50: The citizens' assembly of a township, town, or district shall be organized by the citizens of the township, town, or district. The township, town, or district chief shall be the chairman of the meeting. However, if it is held for the election or impeachment of the township, town, or district chief, or other matters that the township, town, or district chief should avoid, the chairman shall be elected by the citizens present.

If the residents of a township or town are more than 2,000 households, separate venues may be set up and held on the same day.

Article 51: The citizens' assembly of a township, town, or district shall be convened once a year by the township, town, or district chief. In case of special events, or upon the request of more than one-twentieth of the total number of citizens of each township, town, or district, a temporary citizens' assembly of the township, town, or district shall be convened.

If the aforementioned temporary meeting is held for matters that the township, town, or district chief should avoid, it shall be convened jointly by more than half of the supervisors of the township, town, or district.

Article 52: The citizens' assembly of a township, town, or district, a temporary citizens' assembly of the township, town, or district, must have the attendance of more than one-tenth of the citizens of the township, town, or district, and the consent of more than half of the citizens present. The resolution shall take effect. The aforementioned resolution shall be announced by the convener.

Article 53: The functions and powers of the citizens' assembly of a township, town, or district are as follows: (1) To elect and impeach the township, town, or district chief, deputy township, town, or district chief, and supervisors of the township, town, or district; (2) To discuss and decide on the autonomous regulations of the township, town, or district; (3) To discuss and decide on agreements with other townships, towns, or districts; (4) To discuss and decide on matters submitted by the township, town, or district chief; (5) To discuss and decide on matters that should be promoted and innovated in the township, town, or district, and to discuss and decide on matters proposed by the subordinate li and lin.

Article 54: The citizens' assemblies of townships and towns shall have the power to discuss and decide on the budget and final accounts of the township or town.

Article 55: A township shall establish a township office, and a town shall establish a town office, to handle the autonomous matters listed in Article 5 within the scope of the township or town.

The township and town public property, public utilities, and budget and final accounts shall be managed and drafted by the township office or town office.

Article 56: A district shall establish a district office to assist the county government in handling the autonomous matters listed in Article 5 within the district.

The operating expenses of the district office shall be subsidized by the county government.

Article 57: A township shall have one township chief, a town shall have one town chief, and a district shall have one district chief, to handle the affairs in the preceding two articles respectively. A township shall have a deputy township chief, a town shall have a deputy town chief, and a district shall have a deputy district chief, each to assist the township, town, or district chief in handling affairs.

If necessary in practice, a township or town may increase the number of deputy township chiefs or deputy town chiefs by one.

When the township, town, or district chief is unable to perform his duties, the deputy township chief, deputy town chief, or deputy district chief shall act on his behalf. If there are two deputy township chiefs or deputy town chiefs, the elder shall act on his behalf.

Article 58: The term of office of the township chief, deputy township chief, town chief, deputy town chief, district chief, and deputy district chief shall be two years, and they may be re-elected.

Article 59: The township chief, deputy township chief, town chief, deputy town chief, district chief, and deputy district chief shall all be unpaid positions.

The township chief, deputy township chief, town chief, and deputy town chief may be given public funds at the discretion of the township or town citizens' assembly.

Article 60: The township office, town office, or district office may have assistants or employ employees at its discretion.

Article 61: The township office, town office, or district office may convene township affairs meetings, town affairs meetings, or district affairs meetings to handle the affairs in Articles 55 and 56.

The township, town, or district chief, deputy township, town, or district chief, and the li chiefs under their jurisdiction shall attend the aforementioned meeting. The township, town, or district chief shall be the chairman, and the township, town, or district supervisors may attend.

Article 62: A township shall have township supervisors, a town shall have town supervisors, and a district shall have three or five district supervisors to report the illegal or derelict acts of the township, town, or district chief and other officials.

Article 63: Township and town supervisors shall supervise the finances of the township or town, and may report to the county government for correction at any time if they believe that the township or town's financial revenue and expenditure are inappropriate.

Article 64: The powers in the preceding two articles may be exercised independently by one supervisor.

Article 65: Township, town, and district supervisors shall be unpaid positions with a term of two years, and may be re-elected.

Article 66: Township, town, and district supervisors shall not concurrently serve as other autonomous officials.

Article 67: The township office, town office, or district office may mediate civil cases of the township, town, or district residents, and criminal cases that may be withdrawn according to law.

Article 68: The mediation in the preceding article shall convene a mediation meeting, attended by the following personnel: (1) The township, town, or district chief; (2) One supervisor; (3) The li chief or lin chief of the place where the incident occurred; (4) One person nominated by each of the two parties. The township, town, or district chief shall be the chairman of the mediation meeting.

Article 69: Mediation shall be established only with the consent of both parties concerned.

Article 70: Mediation shall not be conducted in the form of a court, and shall not solicit fees, receive remuneration, or impose penalties. (To be continued)

Songjiang: Fellow Shopmates Identify Robbers of Rifeng Shop

The Rifeng Silver Shop in this city was robbed at 9 a.m. the day before, and associate Zhao Houzhuang was shot. On the same day, the Public Security Bureau, together with the Water Patrol Team, captured one of the robbers, Zhao Zhiyi, and interrogated him, who confessed without hesitation. The County Chamber of Commerce, at the request of the merchants, stated that during the winter defense period, robbery in broad daylight meant that merchants had no security, and requested severe punishment. The case was forwarded to the provincial authorities for severe punishment to deter bandits. The suspect has made a confession and handed it to the county government for trial. Today (the 18th), County Magistrate Jin ordered Xie Jingshan, Lao Jiaqi, He Pengnian, and Yu Jinghe, four shopmates from Rifeng Silver Shop, to appear in court. At the same time, a team was dispatched to sign and extract the suspect for questioning. Zhao Caishu, a clerk, presided over the trial. The shopmates clearly identified the suspect, and the suspect confessed that he was weak-willed and momentarily misled and asked for leniency. The shopmates were ordered to return, and Zhao Zhiyi was still detained in the county jail. It is reported that the injured associate, Zhao Houzhuang, was sent to Shanghai for medical treatment, and his condition has been good in recent days, and there is no danger to his life.

Car Crushes Chongque Villager to Death

Yesterday on the Shanghai-Hangzhou National Highway, a private car, number 6363, was passing through Chongque, near Zhaolin, when it accidentally ran over an unknown man walking on the road. The death was gruesome. The car was not detained on the spot. Local people telegraphed Minhang and Shanghai to detain the car for negotiation.

Suzhou: Theft Cases Occur Frequently in Rural Areas of Suzhou

Since the beginning of winter, robbery cases have been frequently reported in the urban and rural areas of Wuxian County. Yesterday (the 18th) at around 1:00 AM, more than 20 robbers suddenly appeared at the home of farmer Zhou Xinyuan, near Wu Pagoda in Weijingtang North, Xiangcheng Township, and committed robbery with weapons. Before leaving, they kidnapped Zhou's eight-year-old son, Huojin, and warned that a ransom of 3,000 yuan was required. The bandits went towards Changshu. Also, at Yunjimi Store on the back mountain of Dongting East, rice was dispatched to Yunji Rice Store in Mudu using thirty-five boats, when traveling in Taihu mountain area, more than ten robbers in a robber ship suddenly blocked and looted 200,000 stones of rice, and more than ten silver dollars were robbed.

Wuxi: Tax Bureau Official Assaults People While Collecting Taxes

This year, the Tobacco and Alcohol License Tax Collection Office in this county has repeatedly had disputes due to its attempt to double the tax collection. After repeated mediation by the Chamber of Commerce, it was settled. Yesterday morning at around 11:00 AM, Pan Shusheng and two other officials from the office went to Xingda Small Cigarette Shop at the entrance of Taiping Lane to collect a license tax of four yuan. However, the shop was opened by an old woman, Chen Zhang, with a small capital and bleak business. Her daily sales profit was less than one yuan, and it was extremely difficult to maintain her business. Therefore, she requested that the tax payment be postponed until the Winter Solstice. Unexpectedly, Pan and others not only refused but also made loud noises and smashed the large glass on the counter. They also entered the counter and searched for cigarettes in the shop. Zhang was shocked and stepped forward to stop them. Unexpectedly, Pan pushed Zhang hard. Zhang was old and weak, and immediately fell to the ground and fainted, losing consciousness. The police arrived and took Pan to the Second Sub-bureau and presented him to the General Bureau for interrogation. The injured person was sent to the Brothers Hospital for treatment. After receiving a life-saving injection, she gradually recovered. Due to the serious injury, she is still being treated in the hospital.

Six Major River Courses to be Dredged Through Public Works Program

The Construction Committee of this county held its second committee meeting yesterday, chaired by County Magistrate Yan. It was decided that: (1) The six river courses of Beixingtang River, Nanma Port, Lü River, Li River, Changguang Creek, and Chengtang River in Xizhang section should be dredged through public works program first. In addition to the 15,000 yuan applied to the province for approval, 4,000 yuan should be allocated from the county's water conservancy funds, and 6,000 yuan should be allocated from the county's construction funds by suspending unnecessary construction projects. The remaining insufficient amount should be allocated from the industrial funds for the 22nd year of the Republic; (2) The construction of the culvert on Lake Mountain Road and the road surface from Kuiyuan to Qiaotouzhu, as well as the expansion of Yangxi Road, should be carried out rapidly by the Construction Bureau according to the plan. The expenses are tentatively set at 7,000 yuan and should be completed by the end of February next year to facilitate traffic during the Five Provinces and Cities Exhibition; (3) Municipal engineering projects in this county should be selectively carried out from the current year's deposit funds, including 1,000 yuan for repairing Xinmin Bridge, 2,000 yuan for rebuilding Jixiang Bridge, 300 yuan for repairing Liangba Bridge, and 100 yuan for repairing Sanfeng Bridge. The remaining funds should be used for repairing roads and bridges in the urban area.

Changzhou: Yida Rice Shop in Douxiang Alley Robbed

Yida Yingji Rice Shop in Douxiang Alley outside Dabeimen, Wuyi, is jointly opened by Yuan Chansheng and Xu Chanrong. Yesterday (the 17th) at around 7:00 PM, after dinner, the gate was about to close, and after a little while someone knocked on the door, pretending to be buying rice. The people in the shop pulled the bolt and opened the door, and two robbers suddenly broke in, each holding a box gun, aiming at Yuan Chansheng and Xu Chanrong, strictly prohibiting them from making a sound, and demanding hundreds of yuan for travel expenses. After searching the account counter and other places without success, Yuan Chansheng was slapped a few times, and then they went inside to search and rob. In the second entrance, they found more than two hundred and forty silver dollars inside the treadle, and then they carried the money and left. Afterwards, the shop reported to the nearby police team for pursuit, but there was no trace.

Nantong: Youth Service Corps Established

In order to serve the society and promote the New Life Movement, all circles in Tongyi have organized the Youth Service Corps, with Zheng Yitong and Jin Zonghua as the leaders, divided into 20 teams. A major cleaning was carried out in separate areas on the 21st, and a general inspection was carried out on the 24th.

Zhu Shusheng Visits Nantong for Inspection

Zhu Shusheng, President of the Jiangsu Higher Court, accompanied by clerk Yang Litang, visited Nantong on the 17th to inspect the Nantong Court, Prison, and Detention Center, and returned to Shanghai by boat that night. Zhu paid close attention to the case of Wu Gui, Vice President of the Nantong Lawyers Association, seducing and raping his niece, Li Xiangzhi, and specially took the case file back for review.

Tragic Murder in a Love Affair at the Foot of Jianshan Mountain

Fan Hengyu, at the foot of Jianshan Mountain in Nantong, his wife, Sun, colluded with her lover, He Hei, on the night of the 16th, chopped her husband nine times and pushed him into the river. Fan called for help, and the patrolling police of the Public Security Bureau rescued him, but his life was in danger. The male and female murderers were sent to the court on the 17th, and the viewers blocked the road.

Gaoyou: Small Steamship Encountered Danger Midway. Gu Zhutong, the Pacification Director stationed in Jiangxi, his younger brother and daughter, accompanied by his bodyguard, adjutant Wu Zhenxiang, and four guards, took the Henggui small steamship of the Fuhuai Company from Qingjiangpu to Zhen. On the 12th at about 9:00 PM, when they arrived south of Yingfanshui and north of Xiaohanzi in Ziying Dam, more than 30 lake bandits suddenly appeared and ordered the steamship to stop on the west embankment of the Grand Canal. At the same time, the Qinghuo class Xinbao of the Datong Company, fully loaded with passengers and goods, was also approaching. At that time, there was no way to stop the steamship. In the midst of the crisis, the patrol post of the 19th Squadron of the Water Public Security Team saw it and fired a warning shot. Afterwards, the entire team set off and fired across the river. After an hour of fighting, the bandits drove their boat towards Jieshou. The two steamships were escorted south by Yan Fei, the captain of the 16th Squadron of the Gaoyou Water Public Security Team.

Changshu: Gang of Thieves, Disguised as Refugees, Rob

At Luoxiang, about one mile away from Shuibeimen, five or sixty guest籍 people resembling refugees suddenly entered the home of Mu Yongxing and robbed it. Fortunately, it was daytime, and a special envoy was sent to the city to report to the Security Team. The team immediately ordered the entire armed first squadron to depart. It was discovered that the thieves were all disguised as refugees and had dispersed. The armed team pursued them, but had not returned to the city by late at night. The loss of the Mu family was about 500 yuan.

Hangzhou: Three Major Shops Close in Succession

The Yixing Hosiery Factory and Yixinxing General Goods Store in Baoyoufang, Hangzhou, are both solely operated by merchant Wu Genxi. Their business has been good on weekdays. Recently, due to excessive credit sales and poor economic turnover, both shops simultaneously declared liquidation on the 17th. The amount of debt is 40,000 to silver money shops, 50,000 to depositors, and more than 30,000 to higher level trading shops, totaling more than 110,000 yuan. The inventory is less than 30,000 yuan, and the accounts receivable from Shanghai Jiangsu are 50,000 yuan, which are all old accounts from previous years and are difficult to collect. In reality, they are only worth 10% of their value. The creditors have held a meeting to discuss solutions. Furthermore, the Cheng Songmao Foreign Goods Store in Bijiaofang, an old store that has been open for 60 years, has also announced liquidation due to the decline in business. It owes 50,000 yuan to silver money shops and 30,000 yuan to higher level trading shops, totaling 80,000 yuan. Through mediation, it was decided to repay 60% in cash and issue Xinglong bills for the remaining 40% to be paid in installments.

Haimen: Wealthy Household Forces Death by Demanding Debt

Dai Zhang, the mother of farmer Dai Guozhang in Andong Township, Fifth District, borrowed ten silver dollars from Lu Tingzai, a wealthy household in the township, in the spring of last year, with the agreement to repay it in the early winter of the same year. Unexpectedly, for two years, there have been successive famines, and there has been no ability to repay. The day before (the 15th), Lu demanded repayment from Dai Zhang but was unsuccessful, so he wantonly insulted and scolded her, and said that he had already reported to the county government for arrest. Neighbors persuaded him, and Lu left unhappily. Dai Zhang was stimulated by this and became extremely resentful, and the thought of ending her life came to her mind. That night, she hanged herself. When her family discovered it, she had already died.

Tax Police Assault Merchants, Causing Market Strike

The 19th Detachment of the Tax Police in Wuling Village, Qidong, sent more than 30 team members to search for smuggled salt at Shen Chunmao's grocery store in Yinyang Town on the morning of the day before (the 13th). As a result, nothing was found. The shop owner, Shen Songru, argued with them and was hit in the chest, spitting blood. Nearby merchants Yu Qingxiang and Jiang Xuehai stepped forward to persuade, but were arrested by the tax police and taken to the team headquarters for detention. Thereupon, the merchants of the entire town were greatly angered and immediately went on strike and sent representatives to the county government to petition, requesting County Magistrate Li to write to the tax police team to release the arrested merchants and punish the assaulting team members. County Magistrate Li agreed to immediately send personnel to investigate and deal with the matter thoroughly. The representatives then withdrew. The next day (the 14th), after repeated negotiations between the county government and the team, there was still no result. As a result, stores in Jiangxia Village also joined the strike. As of yesterday (the 15th) afternoon, the matter had not been resolved, and the unrest may escalate.

Special Feature

Thoughts on Their Friends and Enemies from the Perspective of Anti-Chinese Sentiment (Continued)

However, some specialists have expressed unexpected opinions. For example, Mr. Hainsworth, the former Deputy Colonial Secretary of Singapore, expressed surprise at the achievements of overseas Chinese in his lecture at the Summer School of the Royal Empire Society in Oxford last month. However, summarizing his views, there was a regrettable advocacy for suppressing the Chinese. Mr. Hainsworth's dissatisfaction and over-concern with overseas Chinese can be divided into the following three points: (1) The overseas Chinese population in Malaya is too large. For example, the number of overseas Chinese in Perak and Selangor is more than that of Malays. In the future, Malaya may become the 19th province of China. (2) The interests of Malays should be supported to suppress the Chinese. (3) The overseas Chinese born locally are loyal residents of the United Kingdom, while newly immigrated overseas Chinese are not.

Regarding the first point, the reason why there are so many overseas Chinese in Perak and Selangor is because the tin mining area there is vast. According to the annual report of the Malayan Federal Mining Bureau, the result of the survey in 1930 showed that the total area of tin mining leased land in Malaya was 181,818 acres. Among them, Perak accounted for 114,108 acres and Selangor accounted for 43,681 acres. The two places together accounted for 157,789 acres, that is, 86.7% of the total tin mining area in Malaya. At present, there are no other workers suitable for tin mining, only overseas Chinese are the most suitable, and women are the most缘故 of overseas Chinese. Perhaps Mr. Hainsworth did not know this fact obtained from economic analysis, so he was surprised. That is not surprising. As for the large population, since it is an economic condition to establish a province, it is also a political activity issue. Just ask Mr. Hainsworth, why is Hong Kong, with the largest number of Chinese, not a special city in China? Then, the evaluation of his words will be solved immediately.

Regarding the second point, the so-called supporting the interests of Malays to suppress the Chinese, I think this sentence is indeed a misunderstanding caused by not observing from the economic principles and economic facts. I remember that a British person once said this sentence: "If there were no overseas Chinese, I am afraid there would be no Malaya today." It is known that the economic development of overseas Chinese in Malaya only creates local prosperity, but earns a little living information from the prosperity. Local prosperity is the prosperity of Malays, and it is the "co-existence and co-prosperity" of various residents in the settlement. It ignores the reason why there are so many overseas Chinese and why the place needs so many Chinese. We can answer from many aspects, but in the simplest words, it can be said that the work done by overseas Chinese is not something that Europeans and Americans are willing to do, and it is not something that scholars (Malays) can do. This is by no means our arrogance, it is indeed a historical fact. Mr. Hainsworth may have forgotten and misunderstood. If someone asks again, does supporting Malays to suppress the Chinese also mean supporting America or suppressing England? Then, how will Mr. Hainsworth respond?

Regarding the third point, the claim that overseas Chinese born locally are loyal residents of the United Kingdom, while newly immigrated overseas Chinese are not, is also a scene seen with colored glasses. In fact, generally speaking, overseas Chinese are inherently honest and peaceful. Their diligence and hard work overseas are not only unmatched by any other nationals, but their compliance with local order and laws is also unmatched by any other nationals. Overseas Chinese born locally have become accustomed to a pure and docile temperament, which is the legacy of the innate nature of overseas Chinese. Perhaps newly immigrated overseas Chinese do not understand the local situation as well as those born locally, and they have a thicker concept of the ancestral country, which has caused Mr. Hainsworth to mistakenly believe that it is a manifestation of disloyalty. However, the spirit of adventure and sacrifice brought by overseas Chinese from their motherland, if Mr. Hainsworth can examine it more closely from the facts, he will understand that overseas Chinese are helpful to British rule. (To be continued)

Ten years ago, the silver reserves in Shanghai were much less than they are now, but there were no chaotic phenomena at that time, which is clear evidence. The Harvard Ship Has Completely Sunk

Norwegian Consulate Received Witness Testimony Yesterday

Insurance Company Salvages Foreign Rice

Guowen News Agency reports: The Tongde ship of the Tongde Shipping Company, which is represented by Dafaxing, collided with the Norwegian Harvard ship, which is represented by Meishun Company, the day before yesterday morning. The Harvard ship completely sank yesterday. The 16,500 bags of Siamese Guangyulong Rice Factory rice shipped to Shanghai Wu Guangjilong Firm are being salvaged by Guangjilong's hired workers. At the same time, the Norwegian Consulate General in Shanghai summoned the Harvard ship's personnel for questioning. The Tongde ship will be towed into the shipyard for repairs today. The details are as follows:

Harvard Sinks: After the Harvard ship had an accident, although Whitedaway Company sent three large barges to tie up to the side of the Harvard ship to increase support and reduce draft, the hole in the bow caused too much water to enter, and the weight of the waterlogged rice gradually increased. Therefore, it still sank yesterday morning. The Whitedaway barge was ineffective in supporting it and also untied its cable and left.

Siamese Rice Source: The foreign rice loaded on the Harvard ship was transported by Shanghai Sichuan Road's Wu Guangjilong Firm, which specializes in rice, timber, forestry, and exchange import and export goods (Guangyuanlong Head Office) from Siam. The firm has Guangyulong Rice Factory and Guangjinlong Sawmill in Siam. The 16,500 bags of foreign rice transported this time were insured by Yangzi, Jardine Matheson, and New Zealand Insurance Companies. However, Guangjilong has not yet received notification from the Siamese head office regarding the total amount of insurance.

Salvaging Foreign Rice: Now that the Harvard has sunk, the rice will inevitably swell after being soaked in water. If it exceeds the capacity of the cabin too much, the hull will explode. Therefore, yesterday, Guangjilong, together with the insurance company, hired four strong, water-savvy workers to wear rubber outerwear and enter the cabin to salvage the rice. However, only more than 400 bags were salvaged yesterday, and the salvage will continue today.

Consulate Summons: The Norwegian Consulate General in Shanghai, based on the Harvard's report, in order to clarify the issue of responsibility, summoned the ship's captain, chief mate, second mate, and chief engineer to 110 Sichuan Road at 3 pm yesterday. The Deputy Consul Jilder questioned them in a quiet room. He first questioned the captain, Suri, for an hour, and then questioned the chief mate and others until 7 pm, when the matter was still not completed.

Report to the Navigation Bureau: Tongde Shipping Company, 131 Jiangxi Road, yesterday sent a letter to the Navigation Administration Bureau stating: "Sir, our Tongde ship collided with the Norwegian ship Harvard in the Huangpu River this morning. Our ship was damaged. The details will be reported after the shipowner's report is sent. We hereby report it for your reference."

Navigation Bureau Inspection: The Shanghai Navigation Administration Bureau of the Ministry of Communications sent technician Wang Xinyuan to Lujiazui, Pudong, the day before yesterday afternoon to inspect the Harvard ship. However, technician Wang has not yet submitted a written report to the bureau. As for the Tongde ship, it was originally scheduled to send a member of the Navigation Administration Bureau and an insurance company ship surveyor to the No. 3 buoy at the four sites in Pudong to inspect the damage. Later, due to the water entering the ship, it was difficult to see through. It was changed to today (19th) to be towed into the old dock of the Coconut Pine Shipyard (opposite Dongjiadu) in Pudong to drain the water, and then inspected again tomorrow (20th).

Ministry of Finance Formulated Transaction Tax Rates

To Be Implemented and Levied Next Spring

Dagong News Agency reports: The Ministry of Finance has formulated the principles for levying transaction tax on exchanges and the standards for levying taxes, and has requested the Executive Yuan to consult the Legislative Yuan for review. After the Legislative Yuan passes it, it is planned to implement the levy next spring. Although the exchange authorities have expressed opposition, the manufacturers believe that after the implementation of this tax law, it will be enough to reduce the bad habits of speculation and manipulation of the market, so they are very supportive. The financial authorities have decided to implement it next spring based on the psychology of most merchants. The principles and tax rates formulated by the Ministry of Finance are as follows:

Two Principles: There are two articles in the principles for the transaction tax. (1) The transaction tax is based on the transaction on the exchange, and the taxpayers are both parties to the transaction. (2) The transaction tax shall be stipulated separately according to the types of transactions existing on the exchange, and shall be adjusted according to the market conditions, so as to be suitable for the social economy and financial situation. The tax rate for securities shall be calculated according to the agreed price of the transaction, and other goods shall be calculated according to the unit of transaction.

Prescribed Tax Rates: The prescribed tax rates for the transaction tax are as follows: (A) Securities transactions are taxed at a rate of 0.0125% of the agreed price, but the number below 100 yuan in each price shall be calculated according to 100 yuan; (B) Gold is taxed at 10 cents per bar (312.50 grams, fineness 978); (C) Cotton is taxed at 9 jiao per 100 dan; (D) Cotton yarn is taxed at 3.5 yuan per 100 bales; (E) Flour is taxed at 7 jiao per 1,000 bales; (F) Miscellaneous cotton, wheat, soybeans, red grain are taxed at 1.4 yuan per car; Soybean cake is taxed at 7 jiao per 1,000 catties; Soybean oil is taxed at 7 jiao per 100 dan.
