Page 10

In the Face of Imminent War, Shanghai's Air Defense Construction is Important

Yesterday's Radio Broadcast by Su Gongwang

Urging Citizens to Concentrate Efforts on Building Air Defenses

An air defense lecture series began on the 18th of this month. Every Tuesday from 4:20 PM to 5:00 PM, air defense experts will broadcast on the China-West Radio station. Yesterday was the first lecture, given by Mr. Su Gongwang, who spoke on "The Importance of Shanghai's Air Defense Construction Amidst the Impending Great War." His arguments were quite insightful. Mr. Su's lecture manuscript is published below:

The Second World War Is Inevitable

Since the "1918" incident, Japan has used its superior military force to occupy our four northeastern provinces, creating a serious situation in the Far East. At the same time, the London Economic Conference and the Geneva Disarmament Conference both ended in failure, and international peace treaties were similarly reduced to waste paper. The order of world peace has been severely threatened on all sides, thus beginning the prelude to the Second World War. Due to the economic conflicts and conflicting interests of the great powers, "war" has become the only solution. We see that at the recent naval preparatory conference in London, Japanese imperialism, in order to realize its ambition to forcibly occupy the East Asian continent, insisted on equal naval ratios, even at the risk of isolating itself and shouting the slogan of abolishing the naval treaty. Such a serious development fully exposes the inevitability of the Second World War, especially the inevitability of war in the Far East. However, when we analyze the internal cause and the results of this great war, whether a war between Japan and the United States breaks out first, or a war between Japan and Russia breaks out first, China will inevitably be drawn into the vortex. Shanghai, in particular, will bear the brunt. In this serious terror, are we willing to be trampled upon, slaughtered, and invaded? Of course, humanity will never sit idly by and wait for death. Not only will we not sit idly by, but we must also consider effective countermeasures to protect our territory, continue our existence, and thereby revive our nation. What we call effective methods here are sound military preparations and strong national defense.

Warfare Increasingly Trends Towards Air Power

However, the form of military warfare has greatly changed since the European War. Because of the invention and progress of airplanes, the resulting development of war tools has entered a new, more cruel, and more tragic form. The space world, which humans once regarded as the realm of the gods, is now unhindered due to the invention of aircraft. Therefore, the current form of warfare has expanded to include the air, in addition to land and sea, as a new battlefield for slaughtering humans. At the same time, the form of warfare has also shifted from two-dimensional land and sea battles to three-dimensional air battles. Past local battles of vying for front lines and fighting enemy troops have now expanded to include all-out battles of attacking cities and destroying the enemy's national strength. Therefore, the scope of war has no distinction between front and rear lines, or between war and non-war zones. The target of slaughter is not soldiers but civilians. Because enemy planes invading from the air have no natural barriers and can penetrate deep without obstruction, the scope of their destruction and slaughter is also limitless. Once the war begins, enemy planes will invade, and the country's territory and people's lives will be at risk of being destroyed, with no possibility of escaping. The American politician Rausell said, "Within ten years, a great war will break out in Europe, most of which will be limited to air combat. No less than tens of thousands of planes will participate in the war. The longest duration of the war will be no more than twelve hours." These few simple words fully demonstrate the trend of future wars and the power of modern air forces.

National Defense's Top Priority is Building Air Defenses

As a result of the development of air forces, countermeasures arise with the times. According to the law of scientific invention, wherever there is active pressure, there is passive resistance. Wherever new weapons are invented, weapons to resist them are discovered. Therefore, the primary condition for national defense at present is air defense equipment. Although the central tool of modern warfare has turned to the air force, and the degree of cruel poisoning and killing is thousands of times more effective than the killing power of the past land and sea armies, all countries are now engaged in air defense construction, in addition to studying military aviation. Thus, they are loudly shouting the slogan, "Without air defense, there is no national defense; without national defense, there is no nation," in order to make the people aware of air defense. Because modern national defense war preparations, if only making two-dimensional resistance on land and sea, and lacking three-dimensional air defense, is tantamount to rejecting wolves in the front and not guarding against tigers in the back. When enemy planes attack from the air, we can only wait for death, allowing them to destroy and slaughter at will.

Countries Around the World are Striving to Promote It

Recently, countries around the world have been promoting air defense preparations as if they are crazy. The people also regard it as a matter of urgency and are vying to promote their "patriotic" spirit, doing their best to assist the government's air defense construction and personal protection facilities. Exercises and training are constantly carried out. The prerequisite for war is how to maintain national strength and place it in safety, and only then can we talk about war. Only by being able to defend can we attack. Only by being able to maintain the country's survival position can we destroy the enemy's combat capabilities. When the war begins, the other side will inevitably take its main air force to attack the political center, military source, important urban organizations, and all war-related forces of the enemy country. If we want to resist and win, then the prerequisite is to have a safe order and continuous industrial and commercial manufacturing, so that the people's hearts can be calmed and military strength can be replenished. Therefore, in the military aspect now, not only must there be air defense equipment, but also non-war zones need sound air defense facilities. If we look at our country's scientific backwardness, national defense military preparations are very weak, especially air defense construction, which is simply non-existent. As evidenced by the Songhu battle, the Japanese army's planes wantonly bombed. Our national army, which persisted for dozens of days, had to announce a retreat and endure humiliation to stop the war because it had no air defense equipment. As a result, the Jing'an area of our Shanghai city, which was the essence of the war zone, was bombed, innocent people were killed and injured, and public and private property was infinitely lost. In this infinite damage, after the pain subsided, we have fully felt that without air defense equipment, there is no safe guarantee. In other words, national defense preparations without air defense facilities are not enough to resist invading enemies. People's lives without air defense equipment are not enough to be prolonged.

The Lessons of the Disastrous Defeats in Shanghai and North China

Although the people of the country have suffered the painful lessons of the fall of the Northeast and the disastrous defeats in the Shanghai and North China battles in recent years, there was once a heated mood of advocating aviation to save the country. One call brought a hundred responses, and there was considerable success. However, everyone has overlooked the overall issue of national air defense. If we want to use our planes to drive away enemy planes, so that they cannot invade the airspace over our territory, and to cover our important areas and eliminate their destructive and slaughtering power, we must of course enrich our air defense aviation construction in order to preserve it before talking about attack. At the same time, once enemy planes drop bombs and spread poison, we must have preparations for resistance and rescue. Therefore, we must not only have sound military air defense, but also universal civilian air defense, so that the people can be engaged in rescuing bombing and avoiding the tragedy of being poisoned, and further protect their lives and maintain their property. Therefore, our civilian air defense facilities are indeed urgent and cannot be ignored in the slightest. However, to implement civilian air defense, the people must know the defensive measures and rescue methods for the explosive bombs, incendiary bombs, and poison gas bombs used by enemy planes in air raids in order to achieve practical results. Because the means by which the air force attacks the enemy's rear areas and slaughters the people are only these three types. If we can have rescue facilities to deal with these three means, we can be said to have civilian air defense protection. Given the vastness of our country's territory and the length of our coastline, and the current lack of air defense facilities, once war breaks out, the entire country will inevitably fall into the hands of the enemy's air force, and there is a possibility of destruction at any time and anywhere. However, the most important cities in various places will bear the brunt.

Air Defense Construction Cannot Be Delayed

Shanghai is a transportation hub in the Far East, a huge commercial port in the world, and the economic center of our country, and the first line of defense of the national capital. If the enemy's air force invades, it will inevitably be regarded as more important than any other place. Then the difficulties Shanghai will suffer will inevitably be more tragic than any other place. This is undeniable. Therefore, given the importance of Shanghai's terrain, air defense construction is even more urgent in terms of the overall national defense conditions. Now the area of the prosperous area of Shanghai is only more than 240 square miles. If we use modern air force's poison gas bombs, using 30 kilograms of poison gas in one square mile can poison all humans and animals. Then, in an area of 240 square miles, only 7,200 kilograms of poison gas can poison our entire population of three or four million in Shanghai. Moreover, the weight carried by airplanes now is usually more than 1,000 kilograms. If the enemy's air force has already decided to come and poison us in Shanghai, it will only take five or six planes at most to succeed. What's more, the air raid methods they implement are poison gas bombs and incendiary bombs dropped at the same time. Then the disaster in Shanghai is even more inevitable. Moreover, when the impending great war breaks out, it will not be a separate war between certain countries, but will inevitably cause a general mobilization of countries around the world, resulting in a human massacre. We know that since the target of the declaration of war is a majority of countries, then the so-called safe area of the Shanghai Concession will also inevitably be at risk of air force bombing and poisoning. Perhaps because the essence is concentrated in the concession, the danger is even more tragic. This impending danger is not an exaggeration. The air defense exercises in the Public Concession a couple of days ago, as long as we explore it from the standpoint of defense, we will know that it is not an accidental action. It is worth a great deal of vigilance for the people of Shanghai.

Concentrate Efforts to Save Yourself and Others

However, this danger is of course frightening and terrifying, but the only way to resolve this disaster is to rely on the united mobilization of all the citizens of Shanghai to concentrate all their efforts to build air defense to save themselves and others. Otherwise, the city's prosperity will turn into a field of rubble, and the healthy bodies of the citizens at this time will be flying flesh and blood in the future. As the saying goes, "Shanghai Bund, Shanghai Bund, will one day turn into the Huangpu River." Now that Shanghai's position is felt to be so dangerous, if we do not consciously and actively engage in air defense construction, the saying may come true. Then, if we want to preserve the safety of the country's territory and maintain the continuation of life and property, we can only concentrate our automatic strength, escape from death, build an iron-net air defense, resist the enemy, and defend the country. This is the only way out, he said.

Establishment of the Customs Penalty Review Council

If Merchants Disagree with Customs Penalties

They May Petition the Inspector General of Customs to Revoke Them

The Ministry of Finance, in accordance with Article 31 of the Customs Anti-Smuggling Regulations, submitted to the Executive Yuan and promulgated the Organizational Rules of the Customs Penalty Review Council. Now, the Customs Administration, in accordance with the above regulations, has designated review members to form the Review Council and has drafted a request form for merchants and a decision form to be drafted by the Administration, which will be submitted to the Ministry of Finance for approval and implementation. The Ministry of Finance issued an order to the supervisors of various customs and tax bureaus yesterday, instructing them to announce it to merchants. In the future, if there is any disagreement with the customs' decision, they should handle it in accordance with the regulations. Jianghai Customs will announce the original text of Article 31 of the Anti-Smuggling Regulations as follows: "Anyone who disagrees with the fine or confiscation imposed by the Customs Commissioner may, within ten days after receiving the notice of the decision, file a written objection and request the Inspector General of Customs to revoke it. If the Customs Commissioner considers the above request to be reasonable, he shall revoke his original decision. If he considers it unreasonable, he shall state the reasons in writing and submit them to the Inspector General of Customs along with the original request for decision by the Customs Administration. The Customs Administration shall establish a Customs Penalty Review Council to handle the foregoing conditions, and the Executive Yuan shall determine the organizational rules.

Status of Rickshaw Puller Registration

The Public Works Department announced that 13,000 private rickshaw pullers within the concession have now been registered, which is largely completed. Hereafter, owners of private rickshaws must not allow unregistered rickshaw pullers to pull their rickshaws, and they must wear the numbered porcelain sign on their left arm when pulling the rickshaw so that it is clearly visible. If the rickshaw puller is sick or on leave, he must find another licensed rickshaw puller to replace him. If it is difficult to find one, the owner should select a qualified person and send him to the licensing office to apply for a license before pulling the rickshaw. The registration of public rickshaw pullers is still in progress. As of December 15, a total of 2,142 people have been registered. For one or two days, many unqualified people were found. After that, those who came to apply for licenses were generally in better physical condition and were more aware of the traffic rules. Therefore, the average number of unqualified people is now less than 3%.

Streetcar Door Closures Should Prevent Passenger Injuries

Chinese Ratepayers' Association Requests Attention from the Public Works Department

The Chinese Ratepayers' Association of the Public Concession sent a letter to the Public Works Department yesterday, stating: "Dear Sirs, According to a letter from Mr. Zhang Yu Xiang, 'Upon investigation, it has been customary for streetcar operators to close the doors only after passengers have boarded the streetcar. Recently, due to overcrowding, streetcar operators have been careless, often closing the doors while passengers are still boarding. If a passenger is not careful, their fingers may be pinched, resulting in minor skin injuries or serious bleeding and broken fingers. A merchant suffered this harm himself a week ago. Afterwards, he reflected on his humble background and realized that his livelihood depends entirely on the income from his ten fingers to support himself. If they were to be crushed off, what would his family rely on? The pain and reflection are still frightening. Considering that riding streetcars is unavoidable for a large part of society, if the door closure procedures are not improved, I fear that more than one person will follow in the merchant's footsteps. Now, I propose the following measures: (1) Notify the streetcar authorities to leave a gap where passengers place their hands when boarding to prevent finger pinching or to install rubber bands. (2) The streetcar operator should sound the whistle once before closing the door and twice when starting the streetcar to provide a warning to notify passengers to be prepared. If the above two measures are deemed acceptable, I request that your association consult with the Public Works Department to notify the streetcar authorities to make improvements as soon as possible to prevent accidents and ensure safety,' etc., have been received. Accordingly, we respectfully request your department to instruct the streetcar company to earnestly prevent this behavior that can injure people's hands and feet. To this end, we address this to the General Manager of the Shanghai Public Concession Public Works Department."

Dispute Over Water Connection Fees for Building Construction in the City Center

Lu Genquan Sues Tan Heng for Damaging Reputation

Zhabei Water and Electricity Company Does Not Charge Fees

Lu Genquan, the owner of Lu Gen Ji Construction Company on Ningbo Road, recently hired lawyers Wu Kaisheng and Jiang Chiping to file a criminal lawsuit with the First Special District Local Court against Tan Heng, an engineer at Heng Yao Construction Real Estate Company at No. 1 Suzhou Road, for damaging his reputation and violating Article 330 of the Criminal Code. The main points of the lawsuit are as follows: Lu Genquan has been operating Lu Gen Ji Construction Company in Shanghai for many years and has a good reputation. On August 15th of this year, he contracted to build a Western-style residence on Jiangwan Zhengde Road, downtown, as planned by the defendant. Engineer Tan introduced the owner, Yu Jinyu, to Lu, and they signed a construction contract. However, on September 1st, owner Yu Jinyu suddenly notified the workers on site that all construction work must be stopped before the tap water is connected. Upon receiving the notice, Lu immediately sent a letter to Heng Yao Company the next day, stating that the owner should be responsible for the delay in the completion date. Unexpectedly, Heng Yao Company suddenly sent a letter asking about the 230 yuan water installation fee. Lu was baffled and did not reply. Later, another letter was sent urging him to inquire. Lu, not understanding the defendant's intention, replied that he would ask the owner for the fee after receiving the official receipt. However, on November 8th, Lu suddenly received Order No. 654 from the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau, stating that the Shanghai Bank Trust Real Estate Stock had complained that Zhabei Water and Electricity Company required the owner to pay a 270 yuan water connection fee and ordered him to come to the bureau for questioning. Lu complied and, after speaking with Director Xu Peihuang, learned that Tan Heng had fabricated facts, impersonated Lu's name, falsely claimed that Zhabei Water and Electricity Company required a water connection fee of over 200 yuan, and attempted to defraud the owner, Yu Jinyu. At that time, Lu immediately denied that this had happened. However, the Public Utilities Bureau stated that if Lu did not thoroughly clarify the truth, his business license would be revoked. Lu Genquan stated that the water connection issue was discussed once on September 3rd by the owner, Tan Heng, and the plaintiff at the defendant's company. At that time, the plaintiff also stated that he did not know whether a fee was required for water connection and that he should inquire with Zhabei Water and Electricity Company to find out. Therefore, on the 4th of the same month, he entrusted Zhou Baolin, the owner of Chongxingchang Water and Electricity Company, which specializes in water and electricity installation, to inquire with Zhabei Water and Electricity Company on his behalf. He was informed that no fee was required, and the plaintiff immediately instructed Zhou Baolin to inform the defendant that no fee was required for water connection. Now, the defendant has used fraudulent means to spread rumors to Yu Jinyu, causing Yu to mistakenly believe and order the workers on site to stop all construction work to damage the plaintiff's reputation. There is no doubt that the plaintiff has never made such a request, so what grounds does the defendant have to spread rumors in front of Yu to have the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau impose administrative sanctions on the plaintiff and damage his reputation? How can he remain silent? Therefore, he is filing a lawsuit according to law, requesting that the defendant Tan Heng be summoned to court and punished according to law, and requesting that the defendant be ordered to publish the entire verdict in the newspaper to restore the plaintiff's reputation." Yesterday afternoon, Judge Zhan Liangce of the Fifth Criminal Court summoned the parties for questioning. The defendant did not appear. The plaintiff, Lu Genquan, and his agents, lawyers Wu and Jiang, explained the above situation and stated that the case was very serious because the Shanghai Municipal Public Utilities Bureau intended to revoke the plaintiff's business license based on the report. Therefore, in order to maintain his reputation and clarify the truth, the plaintiff had to seek a legal solution. Witness Xu Baolin then testified that he was entrusted by Lu to inquire with Zhabei Yongdian Company and that no fee was required for water connection and that he had informed Tan Heng. The court adjourned the case for seven days due to the defendant's absence and ordered the plaintiff to summon the defendant to court for further verification.

Lawsuit Over Embezzled Compensation in the Da De Steamer Tragedy

Plaintiff is a Simple Rural Farmer

Bian Jialu Presents Evidence of Payment

Ping Laiyin, a native of Baipu Township, Nantong, transported yellow sprouts to Shanghai for sale in the winter of the 20th year of the Republic. After finishing his business, he boarded the Da De steamer of the Da Da Company to return home. Unfortunately, the steamer caught fire and burned midway, resulting in the deaths of most of the passengers. Ping also perished at the age of 30. Later, the families of the victims entrusted the Zhenwei Law Firm, composed of lawyers Bian Jialu, Huang Zengjie, and Xu Zai, to negotiate with the Da Da Company for compensation. After being entrusted, the law firm organized the Da De Steamer Disaster Victims' Families Committee to conduct negotiations. Ping's elder brother, Ping Laiyou, learned of this in his hometown and sent a letter to the Zhenwei Law Firm, requesting to register and join. As a result of the negotiations, the Chinese Jisheng Association intervened and received $3,040 from the Da Da Company, which was distributed by the Zhenwei Law Firm to the families of the victims to settle the case. More than two years have passed since then. Recently, Ping Laiyou, the elder brother of Ping Laiyin, claimed that the compensation received did not match the total amount and entrusted lawyers Xia Zukun, Xue Jiaqi, and Qian Ying to negotiate with Bian Jialu. The Shanghai Bar Association also convened both parties for mediation without resolution. Ping then entrusted his cousin, Han Jingquan, the owner of the Xinshun Yuan stove shop at No. 8 Wu Jia Lane, South Qianjia Tang, Huanlong Road, French Concession, to file a lawsuit with the Criminal Division of the Special No. 2 Court, accusing lawyer Bian Jialu of forgery and embezzlement of compensation, requesting an investigation and also filing a civil lawsuit to recover the $3,040 compensation. The court accepted the lawsuit and summoned the parties once, but the hearing was postponed because the plaintiff's agent, Han Jingquan, was also listed as a plaintiff, which was procedurally incorrect. The court ordered the plaintiff, Ping Laiyou, to appear in court for questioning. This has already been reported in the previous newspapers. However, according to the defendant's defense, this case was handled by lawyer Huang Zengjie. Initially, the agency negotiated with the Da Da Company, but without success, and the process was suspended. Later, the families of the victims went to the Da Da Company themselves and negotiated for days, and the secretary of the board of directors of the Da Da Company, Wang Yinqiao, introduced the Chinese Jisheng Association to provide relief funds and dismissed the families to return home. The representatives of the families of the victims also signed a settlement agreement with the Da Da Company. The contract was only signed and sealed by lawyer Huang Zengjie as proof. Afterwards, the funds were received and distributed to the families for collection. Ping Laiyou entrusted lawyer Xia Zukun to send his clerk, Wang Xueming, to collect the funds on his behalf in May of the 21st year of the Republic. The case was heard again the day before yesterday by Judge Xiong Huiping and the Second Criminal Court, who summoned both parties and witnesses for trial. The plaintiff, Ping Laiyou, was dressed in coarse clothes, completely a simple rural farmer, and arrived at court with his agent lawyer. The judge asked him what he was accusing him of, but Ping's language was unintelligible and his answers were irrelevant. His agent lawyer then stated the plaintiff's intent to sue. The defendant, Bian Jialu, presented various evidentiary documents to the court. Witness Wang Xueming was summoned to court and denied collecting Ping Laiyin's compensation on his behalf. The judge showed him a receipt for $40, but Wang claimed that he had not signed such a receipt. The judge asked Bian Jialu who wrote this receipt, and Bian replied that it was written by the law firm's clerk, Qin Zemin, who is now also a lawyer. The judge then summoned lawyer Huang Zengjie as a witness, but he did not appear. The court then adjourned the case for the 21st day for further questioning.

Murder by Scissors Yesterday Autopsied

Police Vigorously Apprehending the Fugitive Murderer

Rongchangxiang Western-style Clothing Store at No. 174 Yongji Lane, Tangshan Road, is opened by Ningbo native Shu Rongzhang. Around 9 AM on the 16th of this month, the store's employees, Zou Huibao (27 years old) and Chen Qifu (21 years old), both from Ningbo, suddenly had a disagreement during breakfast. Zou suddenly grabbed a pair of sharp scissors used for tailoring Western-style clothes and threw them at Chen, hitting him in the waist and penetrating about an inch. Blood gushed out, and Chen immediately fell to the ground. Zou, frightened by the sight, ordered another employee, Zhou Xingbiao, to hire a rickshaw to take Chen to the hospital for treatment. Zou walked alongside the rickshaw. However, on the way to East Xihua Road, Zou saw that Chen's injuries were worsening and immediately abandoned him and fled. The rickshaw puller looked back and saw that he was gone, so he took the injured Chen back to the store. However, Chen had already died. The store then reported to the nearby police station, which in turn reported to the Huishan Police Station. Detectives were ordered to investigate and the body was taken to the Ferren Road Autopsy Center. Yesterday morning, Prosecutor Guo Wei of the First Special District Local Court, along with medical examiners Wei and Zhang, and court clerk Wang Zuyi, arrived at the center to examine the body. Zhou Xingbiao testified that he was 23 years old, from Ningbo, and that yesterday morning, he, Zou, and Chen were having breakfast at the store. Chen dipped youtiao (fried dough sticks) into the soy sauce bowl as he ate, and Zou criticized him for being unhygienic. The two then had an argument and began to fight each other. He persuaded them to stop. Zou saw that Chen was still muttering and cursing, so he grabbed a pair of scissors from the workbench and threw them at him, causing the incident. At the time, the deceased was wearing a wool shirt, a short shirt, and a padded jacket. Store owner Shu Rongzhang testified that he was out buying vegetables at the time and did not know what had happened. Chen Ji, the deceased's uncle, also testified. Guo then ordered that the deceased, Chen Qifu, male, had died from being stabbed in the chest with scissors before death. The suspect, Zou Huibao, should be vigorously apprehended by the police and brought to justice. The body was handed over to Chen Ji, the deceased's uncle, for burial.

Apprentice Burned to Death by Gasoline

Burns Flesh; Fire Poisons Heart

Playful Apprentice Already Indicted

Yang Ahua, a 16-year-old from Ningbo, was an apprentice at the Yuanheng Automobile Repair Company at No. 744, Avenue Joffre, French Concession. Around 2 PM on the 12th of this month, while he was working, he was playfully joking with his fellow apprentice and senior apprentice, Wang Xiaolong (18 years old, from Pudong), causing Yang to fall into a porcelain basin full of gasoline. Yang's clothes were covered in gasoline. Yang did not think much of it and continued to work with the blowtorch he was holding. Because the left sleeve of his shirt was also covered in gasoline, it was ignited by the heat, and Yang's clothes caught fire and burned his flesh. After being rescued, he was sent to the Red Cross Hospital on Route Ghisi. He died in the hospital the next morning due to fire poisoning and ineffective treatment. The hospital notified the police station, who dispatched detectives to investigate. The body was taken to the Tongren Fuyuan Hall Autopsy Center, and Wang Xiaolong, who was playfully joking with him, was taken into custody for investigation. The case was later reported to the Special No. 2 Court. Prosecutor Wang Ren examined the body and confirmed that the deceased had died from burns and ordered the senior apprentice, Yang Guilin, to arrange for burial. The day before yesterday, the police brought witness Chen Xien (49 years old, from Tongzhou) to court and escorted Wang to the First Criminal Court of the Special No. 2 Court. Judge Zhang Chaozuo conducted the trial. Police lawyer Yuan Jiahong stated the facts of the case and indicted Wang for negligent homicide. The court questioned the defendant, Wang Xiaolong, and the witness, Chen Xien, in detail and adjourned the case for further questioning. The defendant was remanded in custody.

Shanghai North Station to Sell Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Third Class Tickets

Adding a New Type of Third Class B Ticket

The Shanghai-Nanjing and Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo Railway Administration recently received letters from passengers stating that the Shanghai North Station only had one window for selling Shanghai-Hangzhou-Ningbo third class tickets, causing delays in purchasing tickets. They requested improvements. After the bureau instructed the Transportation Department to deliberate, it was decided that the number of third-class passengers on the Shanghai-Hangzhou line at Shanghai North Station is not currently large, with about four to five hundred tickets sold daily. However, during the spring months of March and April, the number of tourists increases suddenly, making the third-class ticket window seem crowded. To prepare for this eventuality, it has been decided to add a type of Third Class B ticket and prepare a ticket booth, date stamper, and printer for use when necessary, to improve passenger convenience.

### Wang Xingsheng and Others Sue Datong Correspondence School for Fraud

Datong Denies Having These Two Students

Simultaneously Counter-suing and Requesting Detention

丨The Court Still Needs to Investigate and Reschedule the Hearing丨

The Datong Trust Bank Correspondence School at 128 Museum Road was newly established this spring, with a board of directors consisting of prominent Shanghai business figures such as Yu Qiaqing, Wang Xiaolai, Lin Kanghou, Xu Qianlin, and Gu Xinyi, with Lu Yaoming as the principal, Sun Bingzhong as the chief of affairs, and Zhang Zongzai as the head of teaching. After registering with the Shanghai Education Bureau, the school began advertising for students, promising graduation in six months and collecting tuition fees from each student. According to the prescribed curriculum, lectures, assignments, and other materials were issued. All teaching and inquiries were handled by correspondence. In August of this year, Wang Xingsheng and Wang Xinnan each sent letters to the school's directors, stating that they were correspondence students who had registered and paid fees on February 10th, holding receipts issued by Sun Bingzhong. Principal Lu had also successively sent them more than thirty mimeographed lectures and one assignment paper, stating that the mimeographed lectures were temporary and would be replaced with printed ones in the future. However, after waiting for a long time, there was no replacement. They sent letters urging the school to provide printed lectures, but to no avail. They said that this situation appeared to be fraudulent, and that they were questioning the school about it. They also submitted a report to the Municipal Education Bureau, requesting a thorough investigation. After receiving the letters, the directors investigated with the school authorities, but Lu Yaoming and others denied that the Wangs were correspondence students. Lu even sent a letter to the address written in the Wangs' letter, "Zhangjia Lane, West Gate, Baoshan County," to investigate, but

There Was No Such Person. They concluded that the actions of the two Wangs were deliberately intended to damage the school's reputation and filed a complaint with the Baoshan County Government. After several court hearings by the county's trial officer, the defendants were never summoned, making it difficult to proceed. They then petitioned the Jiangsu High Court Prosecutor's Office to issue an arrest warrant. In fact, the two Wangs were hiding at sea and continued to spread letters unfavorable to the school last month to vent their anger. Lu Yaoming, because the Baoshan County Government had petitioned the High Court for an arrest warrant, also published notices in the Shen Bao and Xin Bao newspapers to arrest the two Wangs. On the 24th of last month, the Municipal Public Security Bureau discovered that Wang Xinnan was hiding in the French Concession and requested assistance from the French police to

Arrest Xinnan. Under interrogation by the Second Special District Court, he was granted bail pending trial. After Xinnan was released on bail, he and Xingsheng jointly hired a lawyer to file a criminal self-accusation of fraud against Lu Yaoming in the First Special District Court, recounting that they had registered and paid fees at the correspondence school on February 10th and that they had received mimeographed lectures from the school, which initially stated that they would be replaced with printed ones in the future, but this had not happened. Finally, they stated that Lu Yaoming's publication in the newspaper denying that they were students of the school was an attempt to defraud them of their money and requested that he be investigated according to the law. Lu also appointed lawyer Yuan Yangan to submit a defense, arguing that (1) the school began enrolling students on March 5th of this year, and the Wangs said they registered on February 10th,

Which Was Inconsistent With the Timeline. (2) All students who paid tuition were given receipts, admission certificates, and registration numbers, but the Wangs had none of these documents. (3) The lectures held by Wang Xingsheng may have come from the printing office or from someone else. These three points proved that the Wangs were not Datong students. He also stated that the Wangs had fabricated facts and falsely claimed to be students and filed a counter-suit, demanding that they be punished for false accusation. He further Zheng Zhang stated that they had been approved by the Jiangsu High Court for a long time and had not been captured. Now that they had filed a lawsuit, he requested

Prompt Detention, so that the Baoshan County Government could be informed and send someone to the court to bring them in. Yesterday afternoon, the First Special Court opened a hearing before Judge Yinghua. The plaintiff, Wang Xingsheng, and his representative lawyer were present. The defendant, Lu Yaoming, and his witness, Sun Bingzhong, and his defense lawyer, Yuan Yangan, were also present. First, Wang Xingsheng stated the facts of the lawsuit and presented the receipt for tuition fees issued by Sun Bingzhong and the mimeographed lectures and assignment papers as evidence to prove that he was indeed a Datong student, arguing that if he was not a correspondence student of the school, how could he have these items? However, the defendant Lu Yaoming firmly denied this, claiming that there were no Wangs among the school's students. The judge, recognizing the seriousness of the case, ordered both parties to leave after explaining that the case still needed to be investigated and that they would be notified of the rescheduled hearing date.

Sassoon Discusses Remedies for Silver Issues

Reuters Shanghai, 18th - Sir Victor Sassoon, Chairman of E.D. Sassoon & Co., Ltd., made the following remarks to a Reuters reporter today regarding the silver market. When asked for his opinion on how to remedy the current silver crisis, Sir Sassoon replied that he knows that the United States now understands that raising the price of silver will not help U.S. trade with China, because the amount of silver that China can export is relatively small. Therefore, imports to China depend on exports from China. However, since U.S. monetary policy requires a large accumulation of silver, the United States must buy it from abroad. The problem seems to be finding a way for the United States to obtain the silver it needs without raising the price of silver excessively, which would harm China's interests. He believes that since the United States is prepared to buy silver at a price higher than the current silver price, it may as well contact the Indian government to recover all the silver that India purchased from the United States after the war at the original price. In this way, the surplus silver in the Indian government's treasury can be transferred to the U.S. government's treasury. At the same time, the U.S. government can make a clear statement that it is not prepared to buy existing silver, but is willing to enter into contracts with silver mines to buy newly mined silver. If what the U.S. government buys matches the output of the mines, and the price it is prepared to pay makes silver mining profitable, then the United States will certainly be able to obtain a large amount of silver without disrupting the world market. As world prices rise and Chinese exports fetch higher prices, the rise in silver prices will naturally not cause difficulties. However, the rise in silver prices must be in line with the rise in Chinese export prices. He believes that this suggestion can be adopted, so that the United States can increase its silver reserves, and China can avoid the same financial panic that the United States has to deal with.

Ancient Military Strategies Published

Modern military books are constantly evolving, and there are many works. However, in terms of research on military strategy, in addition to ancient military methods that can be explored, there are few specialized books. Ancient military methods vary with the times and weapons, and researchers often find it difficult to choose and discard. All ancient military strategists' subtle points on military theory that do not lose their timeliness are cited extensively and included as much as possible. The book is indeed a compilation of the great achievements of ancient military strategists and brings together the mysteries of ancient military strategists. To the Editor: We are writing at the behest of the parties involved. The manager of the British firm, Messrs. Butterfield & Swire, has stated that upon reading the December 18th issue of the (Shen Bao), they saw the article "Thirty-One Cases of Red Pill Raw Materials Seized on Ningbo Ship." The article stated that thirty cases of red pill raw materials were purchased from Butterfield & Swire, which is quite surprising. Upon investigation, this firm sold to a Mr. Chen on December 15th an item that is a type of milk powder, with the English name "National Milk Sugar," which is not a raw material for red pills and contains no toxic substances. It is shipped from the United States to China and has a formal customs permit, and is not a prohibited item. The report's statements are entirely inconsistent with the facts. We respectfully request that you correct the record and prevent the spread of misinformation, thus upholding journalistic integrity. Respectfully submitted to the Shen Bao Editor-in-Chief, Lawyer Xi Ya Fu, December 18th.

Note: This newspaper stated yesterday that the goods were "entrusted to our shipowner Mr. Chen by a certain Mr. Fang, a customer within Butterfield & Swire on Haimen Road in this city." There was no mention of "purchased from Butterfield & Swire." This is hereby clarified.

Education News

Full Text of Resolutions from the National Vocational Education Conference (Part 1)

On the 7th, 8th, and 9th of this month, the Ministry of Education, taking advantage of the National Vocational School and Primary and Secondary School Labor Achievement Exhibition held in Beijing, convened a National Vocational Education Discussion Conference, bringing together administrative personnel in charge of vocational education from the education departments and bureaus of various provinces and cities, and inviting many vocational education experts to Beijing. All conference proceedings have been repeatedly recorded in this newspaper. The conference discussed and resolved fourteen cases, which were handled by the Ministry of Education separately. Now, the Ministry of Education has organized the full text of the resolutions, which is recorded below for the reference of readers:

Resolutions of the Vocational Education Discussion Conference

Case 1: Regarding Vocational Education Administrative Personnel

The education departments and bureaus of each province and city should establish full-time positions for personnel to handle and inspect vocational education. (Proposed by the Ministry of Education)

Special funds and personnel should be allocated for vocational school career guidance and promotion to ensure effective implementation. (Proposed by the Director of the Henan Provincial Department of Education)

Resolved:

(1) Within the department in charge of school education, there must be at least one full-time staff member each to handle vocational education and career guidance.

(2) One or two supervisors or instructors must be designated, and specialized talent must be hired on a temporary basis to be responsible for inspecting vocational schools at all levels.

For the above two measures, please order the education departments and bureaus of each province and city to implement them as soon as possible.

Case 2: Regarding Vocational Education Funding

How should provinces and cities implement the standards set by the Ministry for the establishment and funding of secondary schools? (Proposed by the Ministry of Education)

The standard for the allocation of funds for promoting vocational education should be at least 30% of the funding for secondary education.

(5) If it is not possible to meet the standard as scheduled, please consider the facts and make appropriate adjustments. (Proposed by the Jiangsu Provincial Department of Education)

Resolved:

(1) Provinces and cities that already have predetermined plans to implement the standards set by the Ministry year by year, and have been approved by the Ministry, should earnestly promote them within the specified time limit.

(2) Provinces and cities that do not yet have predetermined plans to implement the standards set by the Ministry should formulate them as soon as possible, submit them to the Ministry for approval, and implement them accordingly.

(3) When allocating new funding to vocational schools, provinces and cities should prioritize improving the equipment of existing vocational schools, followed by establishing new vocational schools.

(4) If provinces and cities have special difficulties, and the Ministry of Education verifies that they are true, the date for completing the standards may be extended appropriately, but limited to one or two years.

(5) When provinces and cities implement the standards set by the Ministry, the Ministry of Education will check the degree of achievement or special difficulties and provide subsidies as appropriate.

(6) Please recommend that the central government allocate 3 to 5 million yuan annually from the 24th year onwards to subsidize vocational education in various provinces and cities.

Case 3: Regarding Vocational Education Laws and Regulations

How should the implementation of laws and regulations on vocational education be supervised and promoted? What suggestions do you have? (Proposed by the Ministry of Education)

Please order each province and city to pay special attention to agricultural teaching and practice in rural teachers' schools and rural primary schools to promote agricultural education. (Proposed by the Fujian Provincial Department of Education)

It is proposed to reduce the financial burden on vocational school students and clearly define the amount of fees paid by vocational school students. (Proposed by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education)

The specialization of junior vocational schools should be as simple as possible to facilitate implementation and practical application. (Proposed by the Anhui Provincial Department of Education)

Resolved:

(1) It is hoped that provinces and cities will supervise the implementation of the provisions in the vocational education laws and regulations regarding the establishment of departments, funding, equipment, and practice.

(2) Existing middle schools that still have vocational departments may continue to exist as a type of experimental school if they already have considerable equipment, teachers, and achievements, and have been specially approved by the Ministry of Education. Existing junior vocational schools that have been converted from junior middle schools and must in fact retain junior middle school classes, and have been approved by the Ministry of Education, may be temporarily allowed to have affiliated junior middle school classes. As for the increase of agricultural subjects in rural normal schools and the increase of education subjects in junior vocational schools, which is a change to a small part of the curriculum, flexibility should naturally be granted.

(3) The establishment of vocational schools should be based on a single department as a principle. Departments of the same nature can establish two or more departments. If the school's economic, talent, and equipment aspects all have the possibility of setting up multiple departments, and there is in fact a need to set them up, and it has been approved by the Ministry of Education, then it may be established.

(4) Vocational school students should still pay fees in accordance with the regulations. It is hoped that provinces and cities will find ways to reward or subsidize private vocational schools with excellent achievements. Private vocational schools that have not received public subsidies may be allowed to be flexible, with the approval of the competent educational administrative authority, if the fees paid by students exceed the number specified in the regulations.

Case 4: Regarding the Establishment of Short-Term Training Courses Affiliated with Senior Vocational Schools

Please allow senior vocational schools to establish special vocational departments, following the example of the special normal departments affiliated with normal schools (Proposed by the Fujian Provincial Department of Education). Please order the provinces and cities to establish agricultural instructor training classes as soon as possible to relieve rural areas and enrich production (Proposed by the Sichuan Provincial Department of Education). Simple vocational schools should be established in the capital and various provinces and cities (Proposed by the representative of Henan Province).

Vocational schools should combine junior and senior levels to suit the national conditions of our country, so as to improve students' technical ability and cultivate them into sound professional talents (Proposed by Nanjing City).

All major middle schools and primary schools above the sixth grade should have affiliated vocational supplementary schools or vocational supplementary classes.

More district and town vocational supplementary schools should be established in each city and county to improve farmers' production knowledge and skills. (Proposed by the Shanghai Municipal Bureau of Education)

Resolved:

1. Provinces and cities may, in view of the needs of the locality and for the sake of finding employment for middle school graduates, establish short-term vocational training courses within senior vocational schools. However, it is not appropriate to establish agricultural and industrial departments. Detailed measures should be separately formulated and announced by the Ministry of Education.

2. The conference recommends that the Ministry of Education consult with various ministries and commissions to order the agencies under their jurisdiction in each province and city to consult with the local competent educational administrative authorities to handle short-term training courses or workshops when they are needed.

3. Provinces and cities should consult with the local construction bureaus, finance bureaus, and other agencies to handle the establishment of vocational schools before deciding to establish departments.

4. It is appropriate for vocational schools to combine junior and senior levels.

Case 5: Regarding the Establishment and Reorganization of Departments in Vocational Schools

Provinces and cities should, based on the industrial conditions and the types of talents needed in the industry in their own provinces and cities, reorganize the existing vocational schools' departments and determine the types of departments to be established in the future. (Proposed by the Ministry of Education)

Please order the education departments of each province to investigate the quantity and nature of vocational needs in their respective important regions, in order to create standards for vocational talent cultivation (Proposed by Cheng Zhenji and He Qingru).

Resolved: The education departments and bureaus of each province and city should quickly establish a vocational education design committee to be responsible for investigation, research, and promotion. Its tasks are as follows:

1. Investigate the industrial conditions, types of occupations, and the talents needed by all sectors of society in the province and city.

2. For the existing public and private vocational schools' departments in each province and city, a detailed investigation should be conducted to determine whether there are any biases or deficiencies, whether they correspond to the needs, and whether the graduates of each department are conveniently employed. If the established subjects do not correspond to the needs, how should reasonable control be implemented and other departments be reorganized?

3. For the future addition of departments to public and private vocational schools, a concrete plan should be formulated and implemented in stages.

4. Provinces and cities should formulate the following three standards when promoting vocational education in the future, design, and promote them:

(1) Establish more vocational supplementary schools and junior vocational schools.

(2) The establishment of senior vocational schools should be based on a single industry and one school for each industry as a principle.

(3) The establishment of commercial vocational schools must be limited.

League of Nations Cooperates with China Academic Work Advisory Office

When China planned to establish a National Academic Work Advisory Office, it wanted to establish a branch office in Geneva. Later, due to limited funding, only one office was established domestically. Regarding overseas investigations and introductions, the Ministry of Education previously sent letters to ambassadors abroad, requesting them to assist in the investigation and other work of the National Academic Work Advisory Office. Recently, the Advisory Office also translated the organization regulations and work plan of the office into a general report in French, and sent it to groups similar to the advisory office in the League of Nations, hoping to obtain cooperation from like-minded organizations. The League of Nations Committee on Intellectual Cooperation resolved to establish an Academic Work Advisory Office and first organize a small committee to collect data for consultation. Among the six members of the small committee, there is one Chinese, Yuan Tong. Yuan recently sent a letter to the Ministry of Education reporting the general process of the League of Nations' decision to establish an advisory office and first organize a small committee, saying that detailed information will be presented in person after returning to China from Italy next month. In this situation, China's Academic Work Advisory Office can have more opportunities for assistance and cooperation in the future. In addition, the National Academic Work Advisory Office has issued more than 1,300 registration forms for investigation and introduction, and there are currently more than 260 copies that have been completed and submitted. The current situation of matching registered talents with the needs of various parties is being consulted separately, and more than 60 people have more promising prospects. The office is currently consulting separately with the Economic Commission, the Nanchang Office of the Military Council, and other agencies that need talents.

This City's National Military Training Association Plans to Centralize Military Training Next Year

Approximately 4,700 Students to Participate Citywide

After the Training Headquarters and the Ministry of Education promulgated the amended student military training measures, from next year onwards, the duration of student military training in high schools and equivalent schools in all provinces and cities will be reduced from the original two years to one year. That is, military training will be received for one year after the start of the first year of high school, and military training will no longer be received in the second year. The shortened year will be made up for by holding centralized training within three months after the end of the second semester of the first year, and all provinces and cities were ordered to implement this from the 20th year. After receiving the order, the National Military Training Committee of this city has drafted a detailed plan for centralized training and submitted it to the Training Headquarters for review. In total, approximately 4,700 military training students in this city will participate in the centralized training next year. The organization of the general team, and the training location has been submitted to the municipal government to contact the racecourse to borrow the field. The nursing training for female students will be held for the first time, and there are many inconveniences in terms of equipment. Jiang has ordered a temporary exemption. Schools participating in centralized military training will no longer hold summer training, but summer training for schools above the specialized level will still be implemented in accordance with the original measures.

Tianjin Education Delegation Arrives in Shanghai

A delegation of principals from Tianjin municipal elementary schools, organized as the Jiangzhe Education Observation Group, with a total of nine members, led by Liu Jingyu, the first section chief of the Tianjin Municipal Education Bureau, headed south on the 7th of this month. They spent four days in Beijing, visiting the labor exhibition, and the equipment, teaching methods, management, and school administration of various elementary schools. Special attention was paid to vocational and production education. They left Beijing on the 13th to visit Wuxi, passed through Suzhou and arrived in Shanghai the day before yesterday. They stayed at the Huizhong Hotel. Yesterday morning, they visited the municipal government, the municipal education bureau, the Public Concession North District Elementary School and other places. At 7 p.m., they went to Jinling Spring for dinner at the invitation of the Commercial Press. After dinner, they went to the Grand Theatre to watch a play. They will take an early train to Hangzhou this morning, stay for four days, and return to Shanghai. They will not stay any longer and will transfer to Jinan from Beijing to visit before returning to Tianjin. A reporter from the Guowen News Agency met with the leader of the delegation, Mr. Liu, at the hotel yesterday. According to his account, there are more than 220 municipal and private elementary schools in Tianjin, with approximately 40,000 children enrolled. Excluding private schools, approximately 60% of children are not receiving education. There are a total of 22 provincial, municipal, private, coeducational middle schools. Universities and specialized schools include Nankai University, Beiyang Institute of Technology, Women's Teachers' College, Industrial College, College of Law and Commerce, College of Industry and Commerce, Teachers' College, College of Fisheries, and College of Commerce, totaling eight colleges. The Municipal Education Bureau allocates and subsidizes a total of more than 700,000 yuan for social education expenses throughout the year, adopting self-study guidance methods and paying attention to labor and vocational education. Vocational classes have been established in two elementary schools for experimentation. Although the equipment of each school cannot be said to be perfect, it is getting better year by year, because each school is allocated 50 to 60 yuan of equipment fees per month, which are used exclusively for purchasing educational supplies and references, such as instruments, models, and specimen supplies. The current Education Department has decided on a future policy to restrict and merge existing middle school classes, and expand vocational education. On the one hand, this will enable more school-age children to have the opportunity to attend school, and on the other hand, it will enable students in school to acquire considerable life skills, because most middle school graduates in Tianjin cannot continue their education and feel a sense of unemployment panic.

Education Bureau Orders Elementary Schools to Pay Attention to Preventing Students at Renhui Elementary School from Being Swindled out of Jewelry

The Shanghai Municipal Education Bureau issued a special order to public and private elementary schools yesterday regarding the incident of students at Renhui Elementary School being swindled out of jewelry: According to the report submitted by Pan Renwei, the principal of Renhui Elementary School, Chai Yongkang, the brother of Chai Xingju, a female student in the first grade of the school, came to the school on the afternoon of December 4th and claimed that his sister Xingju was on her way home from school on the morning of that day when she suddenly met a person claiming to be Xingju's father, who ordered her to accompany him home. He also said that she should take off the gold rings she was wearing on her ears, fearing they might be lost, and wrap them in a handkerchief and hide them in her pocket. However, when she wrapped them in the handkerchief, the swindler took the opportunity to steal them. Xingju was young and ignorant and believed it to be true, and was thus swindled out of a pair of gold rings. The school requests that the school pay attention to the matter. The situation has been reported to the Mongol Road Police Station, and the school has also notified the families of the students to pay attention. Therefore, the city is a place where people from all walks of life gather, and such villains are certainly not few. If precautions are not taken in advance, it is feared that similar incidents will occur in other schools. In view of the above situation, in addition to sending a letter to the Public Security Bureau ordering the police to investigate and arrest them at any time, the schools are hereby ordered to admonish the students and notify their families to pay attention to prevention. This is the order.

The Main Player Was Penalized Out, Jiangwan Lost Sadly

Leading All the Way, Success Failed at the Last Moment

Four to Five, Forty-Three to Forty-Five, Lost by Two Points

Jiangwan met with McCray last night in the Group A competition of the West China YMCA basketball league. Jiangwan performed exceptionally well, and the intensity of the competition was truly rare this season. At the beginning of the first half, McCray took the lead with 4-0 and 6-1. Jiangwan's slight setback was mainly due to Zhou Dayun and Chen Zongqi both being penalized off the court, resulting in a significant loss of vitality. In the second half, the two sides were even closer, with the score fluctuating unpredictably. Jiangwan had twice taken the lead by one point. When the final score reached 43-42, Zhang Jinhua was also penalized off the court for committing four fouls. As a result, McCray seized the opportunity to launch a fierce attack, first tying the score at 43-43. With one minute remaining, McCray's Johnson made a close shot, resulting in Jiangwan suffering a defeat with a score of 45-43, a difference of two points. In another match, Jinan decisively defeated Chi Chih, with the situation leaning heavily to one side, the score being 69-19.

Ended in a 3-3 Draw

Only Played 25 Minutes in the Second Half

The intercollegiate football match between St. John's University and Shanghai University was held at Shen Park yesterday afternoon for the third final. Qian is indeed a famous player from Donghua in the past. The wingers are weak, relying entirely on the three people in the middle. Spring and Autumn

Little Western Paradise

— By Zhang Henshui

Chapter Six: A Poor Girl Should Not Be Ashamed to Take on the Role of a Teacher, and a Tutor Is Not Worth Respecting; Empty Humility Is in Vain

So, amidst Hu's repeated urgings to "stand up, stand up," she truly stood up. Unknowingly, she had taken the cigarette in her hand. She didn't know how to smoke and didn't dare put it down, so she held the cigarette without knowing what to do with it. Moreover, she and Jia Duocai were standing very close, almost within breathing distance. The closer they were, the more restless Jia Duocai became, staring intently at Yueying's face. He wasn't nearsighted and needed to see her up close; he wanted to take this opportunity to examine Yueying's skin closely. Poor Yueying, unable to be embarrassed, had to blush and let him stare. Hu chuckled, "What are you doing standing there like a fool? Bring the cigarette to Master Jia's mouth and light it for him. You need to know that a concubine serves her master like this." Yueying, unable to defy her words, had to do as she was told. She brought the cigarette to Jia Duocai's mouth, and he indeed leaned over, holding the cigarette butt in his mouth, naturally with a smile on his face. He held the table, and there was a box of matches nearby. He picked it up, struck a match, and reached out to light the cigarette. Of course, this was an amateurish gesture. Jia Duocai reached out and held her hand, flattening it, before lighting the cigarette. He smiled and released her hand, saying, "Next time you light a cigarette, you have to learn this way, or you'll burn the smoker's eyebrows off." Yueying was afraid of him staring at her face, and he actually held her hand, so she could only endure the embarrassment. Hu, seeing this, chimed in, "Does that mean Master Jia agrees to this matter?" Jia Duocai laughed, "What makes you think I agree?" Hu smiled, "Didn't you say that in the future, she'll have to light your cigarettes this way?" Jia Duocai laughed, "I'm just saying that as an example. If you're all willing to do as I say, then this is settled." (93)

Slaughterhouse

— Zhu Ying

On that wide road stands a tall steel-and-concrete factory, surrounded by a low wall. Blood, diluted by water and turned light red, flows incessantly from the drains outside.

This is a slaughterhouse, the central mechanism supplying fresh beef to every market in the city.

It is said that each cow, in the slaughtering machine, takes no more than two minutes not only to lose its life and have its skin completely peeled off, but also to have its heart, liver, and stomach prepared, and its entire body dismembered and washed clean. Slaughtering cows with such a machine's swift actions is said to be humane, because it is naturally much better than slaughtering cows in the old way, where each cow suffered dozens of cuts before dying.

But as I pass the slaughterhouse every day, I often see groups of cows being led into the slaughterhouse by their owners to await their execution. Strangely, every cow slows down its pace about ten yards from the slaughterhouse door, refusing to walk. The owners whip them constantly, but after being whipped, they take two steps and then stop again. Some simply kneel on the ground, refusing to stand up. Some even shed tears from their eyes and cry out incessantly, as if they know that their lives are about to end.

The mischievous children wait for the arrival of the cows every day, using small bamboo sticks to hit the cows' rumps for amusement. But when the cows kneel on the ground and cry out, they are stunned, unknowingly dropping their small bamboo sticks on the ground. Only after the owners forcefully pull the cows one by one into the steel-and-concrete slaughterhouse do they walk away listlessly.

Not long after, bloody water from the drains flows out again, and after a while, chunks of beef steaming with heat are loaded onto trucks and sent to the markets for sale.

Then, another group of cows waiting to be slaughtered arrives at the door.

Not only do they keep their hands in their sleeves, but they also like to tie up their trouser legs, so when something happens, everyone is "bound and unable to move forward."

Mr. Thick-Skinned

— Chen Liang

I have many eccentric friends, and Mr. Thick-Skinned is one of them. Mr.'s original surname was Zou. His father died suddenly of illness, and his mother remarried a Mr. Huang, so he followed her in taking the surname Huang. Some people criticized him for this, and he angrily retorted, "This is my filial piety, repaying my mother's kindness. It is also my freedom. Even if I take the surname Zhang, Zheng, Li, or Zhao, no one has the right to interfere!" Everyone was speechless, smiled secretly, and retreated. This is how the name "Thick-Skinned" came about.

Mr.'s appearance is not different from ordinary people, but it is also unique. His nose is flat and large, his eyes are round and small like a rat's, his lips are thick and wide, and he looks like he is eating people when he smiles. His face is round, which is originally a sign of wealth, but the three or five pockmarks near his temples spoil the feng shui. His eyebrows are thick and black, slightly fierce, so the expression on his face is often awkward. His friends are happy to associate with him because he is generally honest and kind. However, Mr. is indeed an amorous person who often asks his friends to act as matchmakers for him, and he takes large group photos and distributes them like flyers. Once, a certain organization held a meeting, and there was a female member. Mr. immediately, in the name of Representative X Committee Member, showed great enthusiasm towards her, helping her take off her coat and change her handkerchief. He first presented her with a card, then showed her his works. Later, the woman had a sudden urge to use the restroom, and he volunteered to be her guide, unexpectedly taking her directly to the inner room, where he was shouted out by other female guests using the restroom, and he instead accused the female guests of being old-fashioned. Thus, the name "Thick-Skinned" spread even more widely.

One day, I was entertaining two of my wife's brothers at home. There were four kinds of cold dishes and two pounds of Shaoxing wine. Just as we were about to pick up our chopsticks, Mr. Thick-Skinned arrived. I quickly pulled him to the side room and told him that today was a family gathering for my relatives and that it was not convenient to invite Mr. to be an intimate guest, and I hinted that he should leave quickly. But he was unmoved and insisted that I introduce him. Helpless, I had to quickly invite him to sit down. Before I could even say a word, his chopsticks were already moving like raindrops, eating and saying, "Life in this world is all empty. Only eating is the most practical. I believe that eating is my life's purpose. Even when I die, I don't need a coffin." Coincidentally, at this time, the neighbor woman was scolding a cat that was stealing food, "You beast, tomorrow I'll buy a bag of arsenic to poison you to death!" Mr. Thick-Skinned seemed to sense something and left before the end of the meal.

The next morning, a letter arrived, saying, "Yesterday, when I went to the back door, I realized that I had misunderstood the scolding. I thought about going back in, but it seemed to involve face, because there were your relatives present. It's a pity that I didn't get to gorge on the shredded pork and vegetable heart..." His thick skin was such that one could only sigh in admiration. Therefore, I wrote "Mr. Thick-Skinned" to promote benevolence!

— Yin Juan

Some use force to destroy peace, and others use force to deal with those who destroy peace; in the end, peace is always lost!

Pawnshops in Europe and America (Continued)

— Fang Zhengping

Germany

In Germany, in addition to private pawnshops, there are state-run, city-town-village-run, and public organization-run public pawnshops. The capital is subsidized by the organizers and does not rely on fundraising. The interest rate is from 6% to 12%, while private pawnshops charge from 12% to 24% annual interest. The term is half a year to a year, and if one is unable to redeem the item at the time, one can pay in installments. After the term expires, the item can be auctioned off immediately. Before the sale, the pawnor can redeem the item by paying a special handling fee. If there is a surplus after the sale, it must be returned to the pawnor. The authorities are responsible for compensating for any loss of the item.

(7) Austria

Austria's public pawnshop industry is similar to that of Germany. The loan interest rate is from 5% to 10% annual interest. The smaller the pawn amount, the lower the interest rate charged, which is its characteristic. The term is also usually one year, and the liability for compensation is the same as in Germany.

Records of Faint Fragrance

— Originally written by Princess Der Ling of Qing, translated by Qin Shouou

Chapter Nineteen: Fox Immortal Pagoda

"Today, we must take a trip to the Fox Immortal Pagoda; it is also a very famous place!" After our visit to the relics of the past emperors, the Empress Dowager's melancholy had lessened considerably the next morning. After getting dressed, she planned to go out for a tour. Her actions were, of course, absolutely free. She did not need to ask for our consent and could take us wherever she pleased, but she often liked to show off her own knowledge. Whenever something new happened, or before going to a new place, she would always tell us some general information first. At this time, she told us as usual: "We have heard about the story of the Fox Immortal for a long time! This Fox Immortal Pagoda is the place of cultivation after repentance. Now that we have arrived in Fengtian, we must take a trip, or it would be a pity!"

"Then, what is its story?" We asked her for details, partly driven by curiosity and partly to amuse her.

She smiled very proudly and immediately agreed to tell us. In fact, even if we didn't ask, she would definitely tell us automatically. So we heard a story about the thousand-year-old nine-tailed fox that we had never heard before. The following are the words of the Empress Dowager:

"Before this Fox Immortal was born as a fox, what kind of beast it was, no one can answer. Even the Jade Emperor in heaven probably couldn't say. Everyone only knows that its previous life must have been a very fierce and terrible thing, which was only harmful and not beneficial to humans. But the detailed situation is not clear." (203)

Local Customs

One Aspect of Shanghai's Wartime Literature

— Shanghai News Agency

丨丨 Poems about the Opium War

Those who have an accurate understanding of Shanghai's history are well aware of the relationship between the Opium War and Shanghai. Now that we revisit the past, we cannot help but sigh at the Qing government's ignorance and incompetence. Nevertheless, the battle of Wusong is a tragic and magnificent historical event. The poems that have been passed down, describing the turmoil of the time, still make us feel the greatness of those "national heroes" when we read them today.

On June 9, 1842, British warships arrived near the Wusong estuary. Governor Niu Jian was stationed in Baoshan City, Jiangnan Admiral Chen Huacheng was stationed at the West Fort, the Xuzhou Garrison General was stationed at Xiaoshabei, and Acting General Zhou Shirong was stationed at the East Fort. On the 12th, the British troops advanced in a line of ships, and our army waited in full battle array. The tense situation at that time was truly as Yang Jinjie described:

"Clouds darken, morning sprinkles with tears of thousands;

Moon chills, night submerges in smoke from ten thousand stoves."

And as Jiang Dunfu said in "Ode to General Yingchuan":

"Towering giant cannons on the east and west platforms, towering ships cross the sea, wind and smoke arise,

This is the golden key to Jiangnan, ushering in ten thousand miles of peace."

On the 16th, the battle began. Chen Huacheng opened fire against the enemy, causing significant casualties to the enemy forces. Later, the enemy attacked the East Fort and Xiaoshabei. The troops at Xiaoshabei retreated first, and the troops at the East Fort then collapsed. Niu Jian abandoned the city and fled, and Baoshan City fell into the hands of the British. However, the West Fort still resisted with all its might until death, and as a result, Admiral Chen and eighty others died in battle.

Bei Qingqiao, a famous scholar from Suzhou, once wrote a satirical poem about the event:

"Sea mirage demons press against the flagpoles, eagerly watching the ax-wielding valiant ones.

The unwavering spirit of Suiyang can become a vengeful ghost, a sword should first be used to behead Helan."

Jiang Dunfu also said:

"How can there be strategic planning worthy of a commander, merely laborious tiger servants misleading military planning.

All matters have always been marred by interference, such a strategic pass is lost!"

They all expressed dissatisfaction with Niu Jian, who was called "Governor", and praised Chen Huacheng's bravery and courage. Bei Qingqiao even more forcefully expressed this in the poem "Visiting the Memorial Temple of Duke Zhongmin Chen in Hudou", as follows:

"In the first battle at the Yongjiang estuary, the governor died, the admiral fled. In the second battle at the Wusong estuary, the admiral died, the governor fled. The third battle reached the city of Jinling, the river waves are silent, no sound is heard. After General Chen, who dares to send troops? Do you not see that those who fled are abandoned in the market, those who died live on forever. Live on forever, their spirits are revered by the people of the coast."

Originally, after the British army captured Wusong and Shanghai, they could sail up the Yangtze River, capture Zhenjiang, and threaten Nanjing. As a result, the Qing court endured humiliation and negotiated peace, and the Treaty of Nanjing was signed, opening Shanghai as a treaty port. (The establishment of the concessions was another matter.) Jiang Dunfu expressed deep feelings in his poem, saying:

"Defeat was reported on the riverbank, news spread, but not all was true.

Basha and Jimen were like child's play, Xiao Niang and Lü Mu each escaped unscathed.

I heard that trade has already begun this year, the court itself plans for the people's livelihood.

When the decree to demarcate concessions was issued, ten thousand people rejoiced, but pitiful were the good families of the six prefectures."

In this battle, apart from Chen Huacheng and others, only Yang Qing'en, the registrar of Shanghai, died in the fighting among the local officials in Shanghai, and only Li Tongyang, the county magistrate of Zhejiang, Wu Shi Yu Fu, and Governor Yu Qian died. Bei Qingqiao wrote another poem, saying:

"Sing aloud the song of the loyal martyr of Linjiang, the song flows with anger, filling rivers and mountains.

How is it that those who sacrifice their lives for the country are mostly deaf officials and drunken lieutenants."

He thoroughly condemned the demoralization of the time and the cowardice of the bureaucracy.

These poems will be passed down forever, preserving the light of the nation.
